Major Flooding in the East River of Guangdong Province 84

Embankments in Huizhou and Boluo Counties Collapse in Succession; Fields and Homes Submerged; Residents Flee the Flood and Go Without Food

Guangzhou Correspondence: In Guangdong Province, before the summer Dragon Boat Festival, there were consecutive days of heavy rain. The East River channel is shallow and narrow, and the floodwaters rose sharply. In addition, mountain floods erupted in the upstream Longchuan and Heyuan counties. The river water was turbulent and torrential, and the downstream Huizhou and Boluo counties bore the brunt. Moreover, starting from the first day of this month, there were three days of continuous rain. The water level of the East River suddenly rose more than nine feet. The eastern and western tributaries of Huizhou flooded simultaneously. By the fourth day, the floodwaters were still gushing in, and the water level rose another three feet. In the confluence area of the county seat, the water was knee-deep. In the city of Huizhou Prefecture, the waters entered homes in Six Corner Pavilion, Xiushui Lake, Bell Tower Pavilion, Blacksmith Street, Ehu and other streets. Residents all took refuge on the upper floors. The areas of the West Gate of the county seat, Huangjiatang, Donggong Bridge, Tie Luhu, and Xiaputangxia outside the prefectural and county seat became a vast expanse of water. Boats were used for travel, and the ripening rice paddies and miscellaneous grains were all submerged. The harvest for this season is hopeless, and the impact has caused rice prices to soar more than twofold. The poor are all crying out in pain. Late at night on the second, the waters were particularly turbulent. The embankment of Hongteng Township in the Seventh District was breached by the raging current, with a gap of several dozen feet. Villagers inside the embankment were unable to escape in time, and dozens drowned. Countless houses collapsed. The floodwaters also affected nearby Aibei Township, and the villagers fled to the hills for refuge, sleeping in the open air and eating in the wind. At this time, when the old crop has been exhausted and the new one not yet harvested, many people are lamenting that they have no food. The terrain of Boluo County is also low-lying and located in the downstream basin of the East River. By the fourth day, the floodwaters had arrived, and all of the Shangshui Guan, Xiashui Guan, Da Xi Men, and Xiao Xi Men were submerged. The raging current was so rapid that small boats could not pass. Only the Da Dong Men and Xiao Dong Men could be used for travel by boat. The water level inside the city was higher than in Huizhou. On the fifth day, the waters completely flooded Lu Zu Lane, Xianji Street, Jiali Street, Tangbei Lane, and Houjie Hengjie, with the floodwaters reaching the eaves. If they rose by another foot, the buildings in that area would be submerged in the water. Micang Lane, Qiaotou Lane, Shigu Lane, and Huangwu Lane, which are located on higher ground, were also several feet deep in water. Dozens of villages and towns outside Boluo, such as Sucunwei, Baizuling, Erhewu, Licunwei, and Dalongwei have become a marsh. Dozens of feet of the levee collapsed in Qiankou of Shuixiang. More than a dozen floating corpses have been found in the river near Licun in the past few days. Many houses have collapsed nearby. Furthermore, on the third day, the houses of five residents near Shuikouwei in the Seventh District of Huizhou were washed away by the water, and several people drowned. In addition, boats sink on the river every day, and small boats do not dare to travel. Various highways in Huizhou, such as the Huishan, Huibo, Huizi, Huijia, and Huilong sections, have all been blocked by water, and traffic has been suspended. (June 6th)

Shantou's Silver Shortage 85

All Industries and Businesses Are at a Standstill; Guangdong Province Will Take the Opportunity to Switch to the Dollar Standard

Shantou Correspondence: The financial crisis in Shantou has become increasingly serious in recent days. Silver is soaring, paper money is falling, and prices are fluctuating as a result. Exchange rates are rising continuously in various ports, and the transportation and sale of import and export goods are severely affected. The general salaried class has suffered greatly, and the depth and breadth of the damage is causing widespread fear. Although the export of silver has been strictly prohibited and the customs has repeatedly made seizures, those who prohibit it prohibit it, and those who transport it transport it. The outflow of silver is increasing daily. According to a reporter's investigation, two months ago there were still more than five million silver dollars circulating in the market. Now, there are fewer than three million. The reasons are: 1. Since Shanghai banned the export of silver, Shantou's silver has been flowing out without flowing in, so it has decreased without increasing. 2. Since the silver supply in the market is extremely scarce, its price has naturally increased, and irredeemable local notes have fallen more and more. Therefore, those with large amounts of capital are hoarding silver, holding it tightly and refusing to release it in order to manipulate it for profit in the future. Therefore, credit is tightening. Due to these two major reasons, a fragmented situation has been formed. (At the end of last month, because the Shantou branch of the Provincial Bank exported a large amount of silver, the price of silver soared, rising to 1.3 yuan. For example, one silver dollar was equivalent to 1.3 yuan of guaranteed banknotes denominated in silver in Shantou. The price of small silver coins also increased with the price of silver. Every yuan of guaranteed banknotes was only worth 91 cents of small silver coins. After merchants protested, the Shantou branch temporarily suspended exporting silver, and the price of silver fell slightly as a result, falling to just over 1.2 yuan per yuan. On the 3rd of this month, a certain party bought silver again on a large scale. Those who owned silver seized the opportunity to hold on tightly, and the price of silver rose again from exhaustion, breaking an unprecedented record. On the 3rd, it rose to more than 1.31 yuan. On the morning of the 4th, it rose to more than 1.32 yuan, and the upward trend continues. It may rise to 1.4 yuan. Guaranteed paper and warehouse receipts for merchants are falling more and more due to the influence. On the 4th, every yuan was only equivalent to 90 cents of small silver coins. The public is suffering more and more. The overseas remittances that are sent back by the batch bureaus have no cash to pay, causing the family members of overseas Chinese in various villages, all industries, and businesses to be at a standstill. The market at the Dragon Boat Festival is increasingly depressed. Old debts and new accounts in the commercial world cannot be settled realistically due to the cold market. Everyone is living in order to prolong their lives. In the various counties and towns in Shantou, hundreds of stores closed down during the Dragon Boat Festival, and they have fallen into a very miserable situation. It is reported that Yang Dezhao, the representative of the First Army Group of Guangdong stationed in Nanjing, telegraphed to Ou Fangpu, the director of the Finance Department, on the 2nd, suggesting that the dollar standard be adopted as soon as possible because the current dollar has fallen and the price of small silver coins is equal to the dollar. This would make it possible to turn around the foreign trade of this province and foreign exchange would also be revitalized. The original text of the proposal has been agreed to by Director Ou. Ou submitted the telegram to the "Guangdong Economic Design Committee" for review and research. When the Design Committee considers it feasible, it will convene the silver industry in Guangzhou and Shantou to discuss how to change the system. It may be realized in a short period of time.

Northeastern Border Counties Nearly Become a Hell for Hungry Ghosts 86

Most Starving People Eat Tree Bark and Grass Roots; Strong Ones Eat "Everyone's Share" and Loot Grain Carts

Shenyang News: Since the establishment of the puppet regime in the Northeast, there have been continuous wars and famines. The border counties of the Northeast have suffered from severe disasters last year, and are now feeling a shortage of food and money. Coupled with the current high food prices, the lives of the general population are unspeakably difficult. The tragic situation is unprecedented in recent years. Most starving people eat tree bark, grass roots, or chaff. Some go hungry all day without a single meal, and some even starve to death. There are also some strong and fierce starving people who gather in groups of dozens or hundreds and go to the homes of wealthy people in various villages to eat and drink, calling it eating "everyone's share." In addition, some starving people gather on the side of the road and wait for grain carts to pass by, then rob them. This kind of phenomenon exists in all counties. It is said that the puppet authorities intend to use violence to quell the unrest. It is also reported that the puppet Fengtian Provincial Office has sent people to various counties to investigate the population statistics and the production and consumption of grain. According to the report, of the twenty-eight counties in the puppet Fengtian Province, only nine can be self-sufficient. The remaining nineteen counties are mostly in a difficult situation in terms of people's food. Based on the calculation of the province's population and the amount of grain produced, it is estimated that there will be a huge shortage of 55,000 stone of food by the autumn harvest. Therefore, the puppet Fengtian Provincial Office is also deeply worried. (Northeast News Agency)

Shantou News Inspection Office's New Method of Inspecting Newspapers; Editorial Review Committee's Newly Revised Ten Inspection Conditions 87

Shantou Correspondence: The media and newspaper industries in China must generally be guided by the government. Guangdong advocates freedom of speech and has established a Southwest Publications Editorial Review Committee. The committee's review is very strict and conscientious. Six major newspapers and three small newspapers are published in Shantou every day. They are registered with the Southwest beforehand and published under the supervision of the city's Party headquarters. After the inspection, very few articles or small reviews can be published, and the news on each page is mostly the same. Now, the Southwest Editorial Review Committee has re-revised the regulations on bans and has set a new standard, which has been communicated by the executive department to the Party and government organs for strict implementation. If any of the following are violated, the entire piece will be deleted:

(A) Violating or suspected of violating the Kuomintang's ideology, policy, or platform. (B) Harming or containing the meaning of harming the interests of the Republic of China. (C) Belonging to military secrets. (D) Obstructing good customs, defaming inherent virtues, or the teachings of Confucius and Mencius. (E) Containing or suspected of containing facts that teach theft or obscenity. (F) All descriptions belonging to rape cases, whether or not they are rape cases. (G) Descriptions belonging to suicide cases. (H) Descriptions belonging to or containing the meaning of carnal sensuality, or pictures, films, or advertisements. (I) Descriptions belonging to absurd gods and monsters, or pictures and films. (J) All descriptions that obstruct order, such as poor people eating trees and robbing rice. (Note) 1. All daily newspapers, large and small, published locally should submit all manuscripts, including theses, telegrams, important news, social news, essays, novels, serials, anecdotes, health issues, knowledge Q&A, features, supplements, pictures, films, and all advertisements printed in the newspaper, to the local newspaper review organ for deletion, revision, and removal in accordance with this standard. 2. Those who violate any of the above items will be punished separately in accordance with the provisions on publications. In the future, the Shantou News Inspection Office will almost become the chief editor in charge of each newspaper, and it will not be different from a joint office. If the printing presses of each newspaper are installed in one place, they will become a large newspaper office jointly operated by officials and civilians. With the implementation of these regulations, the difficulty of each editor being responsible can be avoided.

Songjiang: Suspect Arrested for Murdering Fisherman 88

Zhu Aqi, a fisherman from Tianmashan, went out fishing with his family on the 21st night of last month. Zhu Aqi went ashore alone to catch loach, when he suddenly heard a cry for help. The next day, Aqi was found murdered. This case has been reported in this newspaper. Recently, the Public Security Bureau has been investigating a series of theft cases in various villages and sent Detective Zhang Yaozu to Tianmashan to investigate. He learned that Lu Adan, a fisherman, was suspected of murdering Zhu Aqi and managed to capture him yesterday. However, Lu denied it outright. Then, people were sent to investigate. According to Zhu Aqi's wife, before her husband died, Lu Adan had asked her where Aqi was catching loach. Therefore, he is suspected.

Investigation Leads to Homicide Dispute 89

Zhu Huzhen of Qiancun, Xinbin South, Fengjing, has five sons and runs a pharmacy. His second son, Qinbo, was suspected of a certain crime and was taken by special envoys Chen Zhihe and Min Xiaozhang, along with informant Chen Yucai, to arrest him. Zhu Qinbo was just about to go somewhere when the special envoys showed their guns and ordered him not to escape. Just then, his father, Huzhen, crossed in front of him, and the gun went off somehow, hitting him in the throat and killing him instantly. The deceased's sons rushed forward to fight desperately. When the villagers saw someone being shot and killed, the crowd rioted and surrounded the officers, beating them in the head and face. They were then taken back to the company headquarters by the thirty-eighth foreign bridge gendarmerie and transferred to the county government. Zhu Qinbo was also taken to Songjiang temporarily and detained at the water patrol team headquarters. The injured special envoys have been examined by the prosecutor's office and are now being treated at Songjiang Hospital.

Fengxian: Hoppers Found on the Seawall in the County 90

Hoppers have been found in the reed marshes outside the seawall in the eighth district, Nancheng, Pengzhen, Xiaotan, and other townships of the neighboring Nanhui County, causing significant damage, covering an area of 1,000 mu. Recently, they have also been found outside the seawall in this county. The county government yesterday specifically ordered the Agricultural Extension Office to send people to investigate and take precautions. They also ordered the third, fourth, and fifth districts to instruct the coastal townships and baojia chiefs to lead farmers to work hard to exterminate them in order to prevent them from spreading.

Suzhou: Dispute over Lake Encroachment by Migrant Workers 91

Over ten thousand acres of lake fields in East Tai Lake have been enclosed by embankments built by thousands of migrant workers. This obstructs the water conservancy and farming of the counties of Suzhou, Wuxi, and Jiangyin. Following strenuous appeals by the people's official offices of Wujiang and Wuxian counties, the provincial government convened a meeting and resolved to demolish the encroaching embankments. The Yangtze River Water Conservancy Commission also sent personnel to conduct an on-site survey, which confirmed the necessity of demolition. The details of these events have been repeatedly reported in this newspaper. It is now learned that on the morning of the 9th, the county government of Wuxian dispatched a security team led by Deputy Battalion Commander Nie, comprising over a hundred security personnel, who, together with District Chief Jin of the Fifth District, supervised over two thousand farmers to demolish the embankments built by the Xingu Jiawu Gongcheng Company. By 4 PM, three or four *li* of embankments had been removed. At 5 PM, over a hundred migrant workers who had enclosed fields attempted to cause trouble for the local villagers but were dispersed by the security team. Simultaneously, three individuals claiming to be representatives of the migrant workers arrived at the Fifth District Public Office demanding a halt to the demolition in order to safeguard the migrant workers' livelihoods. Their demands were rejected, and they departed. According to Deputy Battalion Commander Nie, by dusk, over three thousand migrant workers, predominantly from Shandong province, had gathered at Xingu Jiawu, apparently holding a meeting, claiming that the demolition was cutting off their livelihoods and threatening to fight to the death if the demolition continued on the 10th. Deputy Battalion Commander Nie, in addition to maintaining strict vigilance and continuing to investigate the movements of the migrant workers, reported the situation to the Wuxian County Magistrate via long-distance telephone, requesting instructions. Upon receiving the report, the Wuxian County Magistrate immediately boarded a steamboat and traveled overnight to direct the operation, arriving in Hengjing Town at 10 AM yesterday (the 10th). After resting at the District Public Office, he led the security team to Maoqi Port at 6 AM yesterday (the 10th) to direct the operation from close range. Meanwhile, Deputy Battalion Commander Nie, together with District Chief Jin, led three thousand farmers, under the strict protection of the security team, to continue the demolition at [time] AM yesterday (the 10th). Xu, the Wujiang County Magistrate, also dispatched Zheng, the Public Security Bureau Chief, to lead a team to assist in the operation. At 1 PM, this reporter inquired with the Fifth District Public Office in Hengjing via long-distance telephone and was informed that a report had been received at noon that a conflict had broken out between villagers and migrant workers near Nanku because the migrant workers were resisting the demolition. Several villagers had been injured by the migrant workers. The District Public Office had dispatched personnel to conduct an on-site investigation, but no large-scale conflict had yet occurred. As for the demolition, all encroaching embankments within the jurisdiction of Wuxian County have been completely removed. However, the demolition in Wujiang County will be carried out after receiving provincial orders. It is reported that these migrant worker enclosures are organized into eight companies, forming a very tight-knit organization employing over eight thousand migrant workers. Due to the proximity to Tai Lake and the large number of migrant workers, investigations are proving difficult. It is also heard that since the construction of the enclosures began a year ago, there are powerful figures backing them, such as a Mr. Yang from Wujiang and a Mr. Qian from Wuxian, who are said to be the bosses behind the migrant workers.

The Wuxi County News Reporters' Association held its second re-election meeting at the County Education Association at 2 PM on the 10th. Fifty-one members were present, chaired by Sun Dexian. Zhu Dajue, Lian Xiahun, Chen Xin, and others, three people, were elected as alternate councilors. After the election, the entire group took a photograph and adjourned the meeting.

Haimen: Workers from Three Factories Petition for Relief 93

Dasheng Third Factory in Changle Town, Third District, experienced a work slowdown on the 18th of last month due to layoffs and wage cuts. After persuasion and guidance from Party and government agencies, work resumed on the 27th. However, at 6 PM on the 7th, during the shift change between day and night workers, workers in the fine yarn workshop suddenly went on strike, with workers from other departments joining in the response. They also damaged machinery in the fine yarn workshop. The industrial security team stationed at the factory evicted the workers and arrested thirteen ringleaders, who were handed over to the county government for interrogation. At 11 AM on the 8th, over three hundred male and female workers went to the County Party Headquarters and the County Government to petition, demanding the cancellation of wage cuts and the reinstatement of laid-off workers. Commissioner Xiao, Secretary Hu, and others patiently persuaded them, and they gradually dispersed around 1 PM. It is reported that the factory suffered losses of approximately three thousand yuan.

Letter 98

To the esteemed Editor of your newspaper: Regarding the report in the Suzhou and Jingjiang news columns of your newspaper concerning the case of Liu Jianfan, editor of the Jingjiang Daily, appealing to the Wuxian County District Court, it was repeatedly stated that County Magistrate Li Jinfang of Jingjiang was summoned for questioning and that the summons was delivered by the Department of Civil Affairs. The contents of the meeting will not be released to the public for the time being. Discussions will continue today until the 14th.

Seven Public Bonds, Including Austrian Indemnity, Drew Lots for Redemption Yesterday Morning, Redeeming $2,985,000 100

Austrian Indemnity Secured 2-4 Treasury Bills, Republic of China 7th Year 6% Public Bonds, Republic of China 14th Year Public Bonds, Ministry of Finance Military Supplies Public Bonds, Ministry of Finance Post-War Short-Term Public Bonds, Republic of China 18th Year Disaster Relief Public Bonds, and Republic of China 19th Year Customs Duty Public Bonds, drew lots for redemption at 10 AM yesterday morning in the hall of the Bankers' Association on Hong Kong Road, totaling $2,985,000. Except for the Austrian Indemnity, which will begin payment on the 20th of this month, payment for the remaining six types of bonds will begin at the end of the month. The details are as follows:

Attendees

Jiang Lufu, Director of the Public Debt Department of the Ministry of Finance; Lin Jinyu, Supervisor from the Audit Department; Ke Ganchen from the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce; Fan Jietang from the National Debt Fund Management Committee; Wu Weiru from the Shanghai Bankers' Association; Liu Wuqiao from the Shanghai Money Dealers' Guild; Jin Wenyuan from the Central Bank (lottery drawer); Zhu Qizhen from the Bank of China; Mao Rui from the Bank of Communications; He Xiaoyuan, Zong Boxuan, and Liang Yaozong (administrators); You Dunti, Ji Juncai, and Fang Jingzhong (registrars); Wang Huaifen, Huang Qizong, Ling Qixun, and Huang Meizhao (clerks); Gong Baozhen, Zheng Yijian, Chen Jian, and Xu Bangzheng (receptionists); Lu Shuping from the Shanghai Municipal Government; Luo Huizong from the Hankou Chamber of Commerce; Dong Xuntian from the Peiping Chamber of Commerce; Pan Yonghe from the Zhejiang Industrial Bank; Kang Huasheng from the Overseas Chinese Bank; and Jin Wenwei from the Wing Hang Bank.

Chairman's Report

Jiang Lufu, Director of the Public Debt Department, reported, "Today is the date for the redemption lottery drawing for seven types of bonds, including the Austrian Indemnity Secured 2-4 Treasury Bills. We are honored by your presence. I will briefly report the circumstances of each type of bond." (1) Austrian Indemnity Secured 2-4 Treasury Bills, issued in the 15th year of the Republic (1926), with a total amount of $2,400,000. Principal has already been repaid 17 times. This is the 18th repayment of principal, drawing lots for two bonds, with a principal repayment of $48,000. (2) Republic of China 7th Year 6% Public Bonds, issued with a total amount of $45,000,000. Principal has already been repaid 21 times. This is the 22nd repayment of principal, drawing lots for one bond, with a principal repayment of $450,000. (3) Republic of China 14th Year Public Bonds, issued with a total amount of $15,000,000. Principal has already been repaid 21 times. This is the 22nd repayment of principal, drawing lots for eight bonds, with a principal repayment of $1,200,000. (4) National Government Ministry of Finance Military Supplies Public Bonds, issued in the 17th year of the Republic (1928), with a total amount of $10,000,000. Principal has already been repaid 17 times. This is the 18th repayment of principal, drawing lots for two bonds, with a principal repayment of $192,000. (5) National Government Ministry of Finance Short-Term Post-War Public Bonds, issued in the 17th year of the Republic (1928), with a total amount of $40,000,000. Principal has already been repaid 20 times. This is the 21st repayment of principal, drawing lots for two bonds, with a principal repayment of $800,000. (6) Republic of China 18th Year Disaster Relief Public Bonds, issued with a total amount of $10,000,000. Principal has already been repaid 19 times. This is the 20th repayment of principal, drawing lots for one bond, with a principal repayment of $100,000. (7) Republic of China 19th Year Customs Duty Public Bonds, issued with a total amount of $20,000,000. Principal has already been repaid 17 times. This is the 18th repayment of principal, drawing lots for one bond, with a principal repayment of $195,000. For all bonds drawn, except for the Austrian Indemnity Secured 2-4 Treasury Bills, which will begin payment on June 20th, payment for the remaining six types of bonds will begin on June 30th. All principal payments for the drawn bonds, together with the due interest on each bond, will be paid jointly by the Central, China, and Communications Banks in various locations. Please, supervisors, verify the drawn lots and the lot ledgers for the execution of the lottery drawing.

Gansu Province Borrows $500,000 101

Borrowed from the Farmers Bank of China. Zhu Jingzhou is scheduled to fly back to Gansu tomorrow morning.

Money Dealers: Yesterday's Managers' Meeting 102

Discussion on gold bond discounts and improvement of business operations.

According to the Guowen News Agency, although the Supervisory Committee of the Shanghai Money Dealers' Guild of the Ministry of Finance continued to review the mortgaged goods of each bank yesterday, it did not mortgage financial public bonds. The issue of providing loans to rescue industry and commerce is being planned. The details are as follows:

No Mortgaging of Financial Public Bonds Yesterday

The Supervisory Committee of the Shanghai Money Dealers' Guild of the Ministry of Finance officially began operations on the 6th of this month, and on the 6th and 7th, the real estate title deeds submitted by each money dealer were mortgaged at a 70% discount for $2,600,000 in financial public bonds of the 24th year of the Republic (1935). Then, each bank turned to the Central Bank, with a 60% discount for $1,560,000 in cash. Since last Saturday, there has been no mortgaging. Jiangnan Railway Company Issues $3 Million in Public Bonds; Shareholders' Meeting Elects Additional Directors and Re-elects Supervisors 106

The Shanghai-based Jiangnan Railway Co., Ltd. held its second annual shareholders' meeting the day before yesterday, discussing and passing the company bond charter and electing additional directors. The details are recorded below.

Discussed Agenda Items After the meeting opened, the chairman first gave a report. Then, Director Zhou of the General Affairs Department, on behalf of the supervisors, reported on the account outlines for the 23rd year of the Republic (1934) and the certificate of the Lixin Accounting Firm. Associate Manager Pang reported on the engineering and business conditions over the past year. Then, the agenda items were discussed and it was resolved: (1) To pass the company bond charter. (2) To pass the amendment to Article 27 of the charter. (Amended text) The company shall have 35 to 39 directors, elected by the shareholders' meeting from among shareholders holding at least 90 shares. There shall be 9 to 11 supervisors, elected by the shareholders' meeting from among shareholders holding at least 30 shares. There shall be one general manager, elected by the shareholders' meeting from among shareholders holding 90 shares. The general manager may also serve as a director but may not serve as a supervisor.

Elected Additional Directors The additional directors were elected and the supervisors were re-elected. The director designated Qi Yunqing and Pang Zanchen as ballot counters. As a result of the election, Zeng Yangfu, Liu Shixin, Hu Ruoyu, Ying Shoumin, Pan Mingxin, Cheng Shifan, Wei Bocong, Qin Huijia, Su Lezhen, Chang Langzhai, Cheng Zhuxin, Chen Fengzhi, Wu Zhuozhi, and Xiao Jiting were elected as directors. Chu Minyi, Xu Guannan, Qin Daishi, Yang Zhixiong, Fang Yaoting, Zhou Wenrui, Wu Yulin, Chen Kefu, and Peng Zhiyun were elected as supervisors. Wei Bocong, Jin Runquan, Zhou Junchang, and Zhang Shuxun were the next four most voted to be supervisors.

Public Bond Charter Article 1 of the Company Bond Charter of the Shanghai-based Jiangnan Railway Co., Ltd. Shanghai-based Jiangnan Railway Co., Ltd. (hereinafter referred to as the "Company"), in order to complete the Nanjing-Helixi section of the railway, passed a resolution at the third extraordinary shareholders' meeting on December 22, 1934, to issue company bonds. Article 2 The Company, in accordance with the provisions of the Company Law, has paid-up capital of $3,000,000 and fixed assets of $6,000,000 as of the end of June 1935. It will issue company bonds of $3,000,000, divided into 3,000 bonds, each with a face value of $1,000. Article 3 The company bonds are secured by all fixed assets listed in the company's balance sheet and property catalog as of the end of June 1935, with a total value of $6,000,000, as a common guarantee for the bonds, setting the first mortgage right and pledge right. The catalog, together with the deeds, will be transferred to the bond-managing bank for safekeeping. The Company will also submit the bonds to the National Government Construction Committee for guarantee of the principal, and to the Ministry of Railways for guarantee of the bond interest. Article 4 The Company entrusts the bank to manage the issuance of the bonds and to safeguard the bonds' collateral. The contract between the Company and the managing bank will be determined separately. Article 5 The bank, representing the interests of the bondholders, has the right to inspect the Company's financial and business operations, to review relevant documents and vouchers, and to provide opinions to the board of directors. Article 6 The bond interest rate is 6% per annum, calculated from the date of issue, and will be paid every six months. Article 7 The bonds are issued at 85% of their face value (i.e., $850 is actually received for each $1,000). Article 8 The bonds will be drawn for redemption starting from December 29, 1937, every six months, with one-twentieth of the bonds drawn each time, until June 30, 1947, when all bonds will be redeemed. Article 9 The bonds are all divided into $1,000 bonds and are in bearer form. However, at the request of the bondholder, they may be converted to registered form. When transferring registered bonds, transfer procedures must be completed, and they will remain registered bonds. Bearer bonds are purely based on the bond to collect principal and interest. If lost, no loss report will be accepted. Article 10 The Company shall first allocate funds from its income for the payment of principal and interest on the bonds and deposit them with the bank for payment when due. Article 11 After a bond is drawn, the bondholder shall present the original bond to the bank for payment and sign and seal it. Article 12 Drawn bonds should be collected from the bank within 24 months. If they are not collected within the time limit, they will be immediately canceled. Article 13 Matters not covered in this charter shall be handled in accordance with the provisions of the Company Law and related laws and regulations. Article 14 This charter shall be submitted to the Shanghai Municipal Social Affairs Bureau and forwarded to the Ministry of Industry for approval and filing.

The Dutch East Indies Continues to Oppress Overseas Chinese 109

Import of Chinese Medicinal Wine Banned from Next Month; Dutch Merchant Ships to Stop Hiring Chinese Staff Next Year

Shen Shi News Agency reports that the anti-Chinese wave in Southeast Asia has continued to this day and is showing signs of further expansion. Siam, the Dutch East Indies, and the American colonies have promulgated various regulations to oppress overseas Chinese, one after another, seemingly without end. According to reliable sources from the overseas Chinese community, the Dutch East Indies is treating overseas Chinese with increasing severity. Shen Shi News Agency reporters have compiled the details as follows:

Import of Chinese Medicinal Wine Banned from Next Month

The annual import of Chinese medicinal wine into Java reaches 1.5 million Dutch guilders. Because overseas Chinese have a strong sense of patriotism, they believe that Chinese medicinal wine is more effective than foreign medicinal wine and is also cheaper, so it is favored by overseas Chinese. The Dutch government has therefore issued an order stating that Chinese medicinal wine does not meet hygiene standards and will be banned from import from July 1st, forcing overseas Chinese to buy foreign goods. This matter should be noted by Chinese people.

Expelling Teachers from Registered Schools

Although the Java government is not currently expelling people without legal basis, the harshness of its regulations makes it extremely difficult for overseas Chinese to bear. The abuse of the intellectual community is particularly unbearable. The most important measure is to prevent overseas Chinese schools from registering with the Chinese Ministry of Education. The reason given is that after a school is registered, it becomes involved in politics, which is contrary to the Java government's principle of "non-involvement in politics." Teachers from registered schools are therefore subject to deportation.

Dutch Merchant Ships to Stop Using Chinese Staff

Dutch ships will stop hiring Chinese crew members from January 1st next year due to the Labor Party's opposition to the government's employment of Chinese crew members. Each Dutch ship traveling to ports in the Far East employs fifty to sixty Chinese staff members. If this is implemented next year, Chinese crew members will face unemployment. Kong instructed on the Ming Hua Bank matter

Kong instructed on the Ming Hua Bank matter; He contacted Xu Keting, Vice Minister of Finance

Guo Binghe, Director of the Qingdao Finance Bureau, came to Shanghai the day before yesterday to deal with the liquidation of Ming Hua Bank. Yesterday morning at 11:00, he went to the Central Bank to visit Minister of Finance Kong Xiangxi to report on the bank's debt situation and seek instructions on supervision and liquidation methods. China Merchants Steam Navigation Company Develops Upriver Shipping; Builds Three Fast Upstream Vessels 112

Special Beijing-Hankou Train May Not Materialize

Since the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Emei vessel accident, the upper reaches of the Yangtze River have not had vessels dispatched for service, abandoning the shipping industry and causing enormous losses. General Manager Liu Hongsheng has proposed building new fast upstream vessels to develop the upper Yangtze River route. The cost of shipbuilding is planned to be covered by using the remaining funds from the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity to purchase materials, with Shanghai shipyards undertaking the construction. Measures have been drafted, and bidding for construction is underway. At the same time, the company is planning to develop the supervisory board for upper Yangtze River shipping operations, and the business department has sent personnel to the upper reaches for investigation. Details are as follows:

Inspection of Sichuan Province

Li Yunliang, Chief Auditor of the Supervisory Board, and Wang Jixian of the Operations Department's branch office, went from Shanghai to Hankou under the guise of inspection to investigate the shipping conditions on the upper reaches of the Yangtze River, and then transferred to various ports such as Shashi, Yichang, Wanxian, and Chongqing. This trip will examine the entire shipping industry of the upper Yangtze River, laying the groundwork for the company's overall plan to develop shipping and restore the Sichuan River route.

Adding Three Vessels

Currently, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company only has one vessel, the Kuaili, on the upper Yangtze River, and only two other vessels are rented. Therefore, adding fast diesel vessels to the upper Yangtze River is the most urgent issue in terms of business. Liu Hongsheng has planned to use some of the remaining funds from the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity to build three vessels. Each vessel will be approximately 300 feet long, with a draft of approximately 8 feet, a carrying capacity of 500 tons, and a speed of 14 nautical miles per hour. They will use diesel engines for fuel, which are cost-effective and fast. The interior of the vessels will be beautifully decorated. The materials will be purchased from England and then constructed by Shanghai shipyards.

Bidding Situation

At the time of bidding for the construction of these three vessels, the Jiangnan Shipyard and the Great China Machinery Factory submitted bids. During the bidding process, the Great China shipyard's price was lower, requiring 209,000 yuan per vessel based on a length of 300 feet. However, after the bid, the Great China shipyard sent a letter to the company stating that it was necessary to increase the length of the vessel to suit all aspects, and the cost per vessel would be above 220,000 yuan. The company is still discussing this matter because its price is not cheaper than the Jiangnan Shipyard. Once a decision is made, the construction will be commissioned.

Beijing-Hankou Fast Vessel

Mr. Qian of the Malkang Foreign Firm in this city petitioned Chairman Chiang, requesting a loan of 1.4 million yuan from the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity to specially build two fast Yangtze River vessels to operate exclusively on the Beijing-Hankou route. The current two-day and night journey from Nanjing to Hankou would be shortened to arrival by midnight that day with this special fast vessel, departing in the morning and arriving in the evening, definitely profitable. Chairman Chiang specially assigned this case to two departments, ordering the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company to reply. The company has replied to the Ministry, stating that the Emei vessel was requested by the Hubei Construction Department last year to open a Beijing-Hankou fast service, shortening the 388 nautical mile journey between Beijing and Hankou to 16 hours. Vessels traveling this route would have to travel at 24 nautical miles per hour, otherwise it would not be possible. If a vessel traveling at 24 nautical miles per hour were to burn coal, a regular vessel burning one ton of coal per hour would require this fast vessel to burn nine tons. This item alone would increase the coal price eightfold, resulting in no profit and only losses. This is one reason. If such a fast vessel were to travel the Yangtze River every day like a destroyer, not only would the vessel be dangerous, but the riverbanks on both sides would be eroded and damaged, causing even greater harm and no benefit.

National News Agency reports that the Japanese Marine Corps stationed in Shanghai conducted street fighting exercises in the area near Bazidi at the end of North Sichuan Road yesterday afternoon at 1:00 PM. The Civil Welfare Undertakings Management Committee Advertises for Trainees 119

The Shanghai Civil Welfare Undertakings Management Committee was officially established on April 1st. It is currently actively constructing civil housing and recruiting 60 male and female trainees for service personnel training classes. After five months of training, they will be assigned to serve in various civil residential areas. The Association's enrollment guidelines are recorded below. (Applicants for these guidelines can obtain them from the Youth Association Middle School on Sichuan Road.) "Shanghai Civil Welfare Undertakings Management Committee Service Personnel Training Class Enrollment Guidelines" (1) Purpose: This Association has established a service personnel training class to train qualified personnel, cultivate a spirit and ability for social service, and enable them to serve in the Civil Housing Areas of this Association. (2) Name: Named Shanghai Civil Welfare Undertakings Management Committee Service Personnel Training Class. (3) Address: Youth Association Middle School on Sichuan Road, Shanghai. (4) Enrollment: Anyone who volunteers to serve in the Civil Housing Areas of this city must first undergo training in this training class. The qualifications of trainees are: ability to obey the party principles of the Kuomintang, having studied at a university or graduated from a senior high school with a certificate, being 20 to 30 years of age, being able to speak standard Mandarin, and having passed the examination of this Association. (5) Academic Term and Number of People: The academic term is tentatively set at four months and five months, with 60 people, half male and half female. (6) Registration: From June 15 to July 6, registration will be at the Youth Association Middle School on Sichuan Road. Applicants must submit two 4.5-inch half-length photos, fill out a registration form, and pay a registration fee of one yuan. The registration fee will not be refunded regardless of whether or not the applicant is admitted. (7) Entrance Examination Date: Starting at 9:00 AM on July 10th. (8) Entrance Examination Subjects: 1. Chinese Language, 2. Party Principles, 3. General Knowledge, 4. Mandarin Speech, 5. Physical Examination, 6. Oral Examination. (9) Opening Date: 9:00 AM on August 1st. (10) Guarantee: After being admitted, trainees must submit a letter of guarantee from two or more guarantors approved by this Association, pay a guarantee deposit of 20 yuan, and submit a letter of willingness to serve this Association for at least two years before being admitted. If the trainee is expelled for violating regulations during the training period or leaves the job during the mandatory service period, the guarantee deposit will not be refunded. (11) Tuition Fee: All supplies such as lodging, uniforms, paper, pens, and ink will be provided by this Association during the training period. (12) Curriculum: Party Principles, Sociology, Economics, Practical Hygiene, Infant Care Law, Basic First Aid, Family Economics, Cooperative Principles, Speech, Education, Practical Human Psychology Survey and Statistics, Physical Education and Games. (13) Service and Compensation: After completing the training, those who are deemed qualified by this Association will be sent to serve in the Civil Housing Areas of this Association. Qualified trainees have an obligation to continuously serve this Association for one year. The monthly salary is 40 yuan per month in the first year and 45 yuan in the second year. Accommodation is provided but not meals. Shanghai Civil Welfare Officer Li Yinglin.

Ma Yinchu Discusses the Significance of Restricting Foreign Insurance Industry 123

Capital Outflow and Comprador Crimes Cannot Be Denied; Past History is Terrifying and Must Be Taken Seriously

Ma Yinchu, Chairman of the Legislative Yuan's Finance Committee, recently completed the Insurance Law for the Committee. Regarding brokers of foreign insurance companies, they must obtain a license from the Ministry of Industry to operate and restrict certain business locations. He made the following remarks to Xin Sheng News Agency reporters: "Article 19 of the Insurance Law states that insurance brokers and notaries may not conduct business without registering with the Ministry of Industry and obtaining a license. Article 20 states that brokers of foreign companies who have obtained a license in accordance with the preceding article are limited in their business scope to treaty ports and may not entrust others to operate or introduce insurance business on their behalf in the interior. Article 21 states that brokers and notaries may not operate or introduce insurance business for insurance companies that have not been approved by the competent authority." These three regulations require brokers of foreign insurance companies in China to register with the Ministry of Industry and obtain a license to operate. This is not to discriminate against or abuse brokers in particular, but rather to take special care due to the terrors of the past. In the past, countless funds from China have been plundered by foreigners. The reason is entirely due to the sins committed by the Chinese themselves. For example, foreign firms handle imports and make a lot of money, entirely through the introduction of compradores. Without compradores, foreigners would be ignorant of the situation in the Chinese interior and would have difficulty operating commercially. Today, domestic goods are flooded with foreign goods, and domestic goods have no place to stand. Can we deny the crimes of the compradores? This is one thing. The Savings Society of the World, even if it only operated in the concessions, would not have absorbed as much capital from our country as it does today, and the crimes it has committed would not be as deep as they are today. But now there are branches of the Society everywhere in the interior, and all of them are operated by Chinese, concentrating all the capital of the interior in the Shanghai concessions. The investment in Shanghai real estate alone is 20 million yuan. Now that Shanghai land prices have fallen by 80-90%, the Society's investment in real estate has lost 17-18 million yuan, resulting in today's panic and making hundreds of thousands of our depositors bewildered. Who is responsible for this? This is another thing. If all the funds that have been scraped away from our country in the past by foreign commercial banks and the Savings Society of the World were to be used for domestic construction, would it not only reduce the oppression of foreign countries on domestic industries, but also be sufficient to strengthen the resistance to the oppression of foreigners? How different are the advantages and disadvantages? Thinking of this, how can one not sigh?"

Xu Fu, Director of the Fujian Finance Department, Discusses Fujian's Financial Situation: Extremely Stable 124

Provincial Fiscal Revenue and Expenditure Offset Each Other, Construction Progresses. Yesterday, He Visited Huang Fu, Ye Zuotang, Gu Yigu, etc.

Xu Fu, member of the Fujian Provincial Government and Director of the Finance Department, arrived in Shanghai from Fujian the day before yesterday and stayed at a friend's residence. Yesterday morning, he visited Ye Zuotang, General Manager of Siming Bank, and Gu Yigu, General Manager of the Bank of Communications. At 4 p.m., he visited Huang Fu, Chairman of the Pingzheng Commission, who was residing in Shanghai. According to Xu, speaking to a reporter from the Xin Sheng News Agency, the financial situation in Fujian has been stable since the reorganization. Last year, public bonds were issued to make up for the deficit, and this year, things have been smooth. Revenue and expenditure are balanced; although there is no surplus, fortunately, there is no deficit. Operating expenses have been gradually increased, so construction projects have progressed. The current financial situation in Fujian is also extremely peaceful. The silver and money industries are very stable, and there have been no instances of empty accounts or bankruptcies. Xu (referring to himself) is going to Nanjing this time to report to the Legislative Yuan and discuss matters. He is scheduled to enter Nanjing today or tomorrow and report on the financial situation of Fujian Province to Finance Minister Kong. He will stay in Nanjing for about three or four days and then return to Shanghai, taking a flight back to Fujian. Today's visits to Ye and Gu and Chairman Huang were not for any particular mission or negotiation. Since they are all old friends, he made a point of visiting them while passing through Shanghai.

A group of progressive people in Shanghai's educational circles believe that promoting parental education is a crucial key to promoting children's happiness. Therefore, in May, they began to organize the Parental Education Research Association and held the inaugural meeting of the Parental Education Research Association at Zhao's residence in Wuxianfang, Disiwei Road, last night, which attracted general attention from society. The initiators of the association are Zhao Chuanjia, General Secretary of the East China Education Association; Chen Zhengfan, Director of the China Children's Welfare Association; Hu Zuyin, Principal of Jingzhou Road Elementary School, Shanghai Municipal Council; Zhou Junshang, Commissioner of the Municipal Education Bureau; and others. The method is to gather ten young couples to meet on the first Wednesday afternoon of each month to discuss various practical parenting issues, use the Modern Parents Monthly as a forum for expression, and report the results of their research to the public at any time, in order to gather ideas, stimulate enthusiastic discussion, generate practical actions, and achieve the practical effect of promoting children's happiness. In addition to holding meetings and discussions, the association also plans to visit exemplary families in various places, observe visits, study gains and losses, and use them as references for organizing exemplary families. On the evening of the inaugural meeting, the attendees were Tao Shaoyuan, professor of Guanghua University Affiliated Middle School, and Ms. Jia Yi; Ge Liting, Principal of the Northern District Elementary School, Shanghai Municipal Council, and Ms. Gu Jingren; Guo Daxiong, Director of the Shanghai Poor Children's Asylum, and Ms. Zhang Xiaoming; Mei Jinliang, editor of the Shizhao Newspaper, and Ms. Li Jingde; Zhou Junshang, Commissioner of the Municipal Education Bureau, and Ms. Ye Hua, Principal of Songxue Elementary School; Hu Zuyin, Principal of Jingzhou Road Elementary School, Shanghai Municipal Council, and Ms. Zhu Duanfang; Zhao Chuanjia, General Secretary of the East China Education Association, and Ms. Zhang Lijin; Chen Zhengfan, Director of the China Children's Welfare Association, and Tao Shuwen, Director of the Shanghai Children's Welfare Asylum; and others. Except for Chen Zhengfan and Yao Shuwen, who have a friendly and collaborative relationship, the rest are young couples. At the inaugural meeting, the association's constitution was discussed and passed, and it was decided that the following important issues would be studied in order: "Child Training," "Child Health," "Good Habits," "Children's Obedience," "Children's Temper Tantrums," "Children's Fears," "Children's Humor," "Children's Spending," "Children's Toys," and "Children's Sex Education." The next meeting will be held on July 3 at the home of Mr. and Mrs. Hu Zuyin.

Record of the Memorial Service for Mr. Yang Dunfu 128

June 9th was the day for holding the memorial service for Mr. Yang Dunfu, Deputy Manager of the Shanghai Bank. The meeting was held at 10 a.m., and many people attended. After the meeting began, Mrs. Pan Guangjiong first played a dirge, followed by Mr. Zhuang Dezhi, Chairman of the Shanghai Bank, who reported on the purpose of the memorial service. All the guests then bowed to the portrait. The chairman reported on the deceased's life, saying that he had known the deceased for more than 20 years and had been colleagues for 18 years. He had no guile, worried about others' worries, and was anxious about others' anxieties. He firmly adhered to the principle of service and ensured that everyone was satisfied. He was also enthusiastic about education. Now, it is planned to establish a Dunfu Elementary School in Jiangning to continue his legacy and leave a lasting memory. Then, Mr. Kong Yongzhi, Minister of Finance, delivered a speech, saying that he had known the deceased for more than 20 years through the introduction of Mr. Chen Guangfu. Later, we founded the Shanghai Bank, and we felt that to become a modern commercial bank that could truly serve society, we needed talent. Therefore, we invited the deceased to be the deputy manager. Since then, our friendship has grown day by day. We observed his words and deeds, and he not only practiced what he preached but was also extremely amiable and kind to everyone, and everyone was happy to be close to him. Today, the most important things in life are to take the five virtues of benevolence, righteousness, propriety, wisdom, and trustworthiness as the foundation of one's life. The deceased can be said to possess all five virtues. Treating people with kindness is called benevolence; not letting down friends is called righteousness. As for propriety, the deceased has always maintained the demeanor of a gentleman in the past 20 years. He was able to assist Mr. Chen Guangfu and his colleagues at the Shanghai Bank in developing the bank's business to the extent that it has achieved today, which is called wisdom. The Shanghai Bank's reputation has long been known, and those who have dealt with the deceased have praised his outstanding reputation, which is called trustworthiness. Propriety, righteousness, integrity, and shame are the four pillars of a country. The most dangerous thing for China is not poverty but the failure to establish the four pillars. Today, we commemorate the deceased and establish a school for him to cultivate future generations, not only to cultivate their knowledge but also to cultivate future generations who possess the spirit of the deceased. The deceased is gone, but may his personality and morality be continued and remain forever between heaven and earth. This is the meaning of today's memorial service. Tang Shoumin, General Manager of the Bank of Communications; Song Ziliang, General Manager of the China National Goods Bank; Zhang Weiru, Chairman of the Shanghai Chinese Securities Exchange; and Lin Kanghou, Secretary-General of the Bankers' Association, also delivered speeches, expressing their extreme admiration for the deceased. Finally, the family members came out to express their gratitude, and the ceremony concluded at around 12 o'clock.

Heavy Rainstorm Yesterday Afternoon 129

Fields and Land Were Moistened and Refreshed, and the Farmers Were All Delighted

Since the beginning of summer, the weather in this port has been very dry, and the fields and land have cracked, which has greatly affected crops such as cotton seedlings. At this busy farming season, the villagers especially yearn for rain. If there is no timely rain, it will inevitably become another drought. Although the heat has been high in recent days, it still feels cool at night. Yesterday morning, the room felt unusually stuffy. After 10 o'clock, the sky became cloudy and foggy, and the sunlight was completely obscured. From 1:45 p.m., thunder rumbled, and raindrops as large as fists (or hail) poured down heavily. The momentum was very fierce. After about two hours, the raindrops gradually stopped. After 4 o'clock, the rain cleared and the sun came out, and the heat suddenly dissipated, turning into a cool and refreshing atmosphere. According to the villagers, the rainfall was about an inch. Although it was not very heavy, the fields and land were moistened and refreshed. Money cannot buy timely rain, so the villagers were all delighted.

Opened Yesterday Morning

The Zhenru District Student National Goods Exhibition, sponsored by the Student National Goods Year Promotion Association, opened at Jinan University at 10 a.m. yesterday. Details are as follows:

Since the Student National Goods Year began soliciting members on June 1, progress has been slow due to the summer examinations in various schools. The progress of soliciting members has been hindered, resulting in poor results. The board of directors originally set the membership fee for each student member at 3 jiao, and the badge at 5 fen. Recently, it was deemed inappropriate, so it was changed to each person soliciting at least one member in order to enhance the strength of promoting national goods. Today's opening is intended to encourage attendees to promote it, so as to achieve twice the result with half the effort.

In the past, imports of paper products reached more than 42 million yuan annually, and cotton yarn, considering only Japanese goods, also reached more than 20 million yuan. Japanese fish products also reached more than 2.9 million yuan. These three items alone are a very large number. Some people say that China has vast land and abundant resources, but because Chinese people love to use foreign goods, domestic industries are declining day by day. Students are outstanding members of society. I hope young people will rise up to promote them in order to strengthen the country. Finally, Zhai Junqian's speech was omitted.

Lake Society Resolutions: Prohibition of Gangsters Collecting Debts 131

Based on the Proposal of Committee Member Yu Zhongxian, Request the Six Counties Governments to Issue a Notice for Prohibition

The Lake Society held its 11th Members' Congress on the 9th. Yu Zhongxian, a member of the society, submitted a proposal to the congress to discuss the issue of banning vagrants in the six counties from collecting old debts for stores on a contract basis. With the joint signatures of Shen Tianxin, Pan Gongzhan, Yan Jun, Shen Jiesheng, Ling Songru, Tang Chongshi, etc., the congress resolved to hand it over to the Executive Committee for handling. The original text of the proposal is excerpted below: A letter is sent to the six county governments, requesting strict prohibition of vagrants who act as debt collectors for stores, disturbing the villagers. No debts, no stores is a common rule for transactions in inland cities and villages. In recent years, rural areas have gone bankrupt, and the commercial market has declined. Store credit has been tightened. The merchants demand payment of old debts due to frequent famines and disasters, and the livelihood of farmers is on the verge of collapse. They don’t even have congee to eat, so how can they repay their debts? The stores do not remember the profits they have made in the past and entrust debt collection to the vagrants. These vagrants have no morals and are like wolves and tigers with ledgers in hand. They go to the villages to collect debts by intimidating, cheating, and deceiving. The villagers, fearing their power, sell their wives and children, and sell their houses and utensils to repay old debts. Suppose they earn a little after the silkworm season and the autumn harvest. In that case, they spend the entire year's income on redeeming property in pawnshops to pay debts. How can they have the surplus power to pay off these old debts? The disturbance caused by the vagrants collecting old debts is even worse than the officials collecting old taxes. As evidenced by the recent case in April in Xinshi Town, Deqing County, a vagrant was not successful in collecting debts. Later, when he met a villager in the town, he gathered a crowd to beat him to death in the downtown area. I hereby propose to the Congress to write a letter to the governments of the six counties to issue notices to strictly prohibit stores entrusting vagrants to collect old debts, disturbing the villagers, and to strictly investigate and arrest vagrants who collect debts and bring them to justice in order to pacify the farmers and maintain local security. Is this appropriate? Please vote.

Jian De Bank Case: Strict Interrogation of Chai Chuangui 132

Chai was a Director and General Manager. The Judge's Interrogation of Various Charges was Extremely Strict.

The Jian De Bank went bankrupt. The directors, supervisors, and general manager of the bank, Chai Chuangui, etc., were sued by 14 creditors, including Wei Haijiang, on charges of fraud and embezzlement. The Second Special District Local Court appointed an accountant to audit the relevant accounts. After the audit was completed and reported to the court, Judge Liu Yugui scheduled a formal hearing yesterday afternoon. Of the 11 defendants, only Chen Xifu, Ou Jiancheng, and Zheng Huaigu were absent. The rest, including Chai Chuangui, Chai Yousheng, Tu Kaizheng, Li Jingwei, Yan Ziyu, Xie Keming, and Ma Suizhi, all surrendered themselves, which was more than the number who attended the previous hearings. Judge Liu first inquired about the periods during which each defendant served as chairman, director, supervisor, and general manager. Because Chai Chuangui served as general manager in the name of a director, his duties were heavier, and he must have a deep and detailed understanding of the bank's founding process, the amount of stock fraud, the registration procedures, the business situation, the types of debts, and the bankruptcy situation. Therefore, he was questioned repeatedly. According to Chai, the bank's capital was only 100,000 yuan in 1928. The following year, it was proposed to increase it to 500,000 yuan, and it was not until 1933 that it was expanded to 1 million yuan, but only 500,000 yuan was collected. When registering with the ministry, the amount of stock subscriptions was certified by the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, and the Ministry of Finance did not send personnel to verify the capital. After registration, no further shares were raised. As for the accountant's audit report, it stated that by September 25, 1933, the capital actually collected was only more than 250,000 yuan. Since it was based on an audit of the accounts, it should not be mistaken. The court immediately asked that the report also stated that more than 240,000 yuan of stock subscriptions were collected within three days after September 25, totaling 500,000 yuan. However, this subsequent collection of funds was immediately released. What kind of loan was it? Because the accountant could not investigate, you should explain it clearly. Chai claimed that he did not authorize the loan and could not explain it. The court believed that Chai was the general manager, and how could he claim ignorance of such large sums of money coming in and out? Therefore, he was questioned repeatedly. He was also questioned about the procedures that the bank should have followed when shareholders Liang Yaoji, Zhao Ziji, etc., sold their shares and the audit report stated that there were signs of alteration in the bank's accounts. The hearing continued until dusk before it was adjourned. Further verification is needed in the future.

Kan Mengxiong Commits Suicide due to Unrequited Love for a Maid 133

His Foolishness is Unsurpassed. Even in Death, What is the Point?

Kan Mengxiong, from Heji, Anhui, is 25 years old and currently works as a servant at Wang Ji's residence at 92 Huayuanfang, Jin Shenfu Road, French Concession. Wang works as a secretary at the Shanghai Security Office. Kan's mother died early. He has been working at Wang's home for nine years. He is usually foolish and honest. Chen Zhuofu, from Hubei, lives at No. 8 in the same alley. Chen used to be a commissioner somewhere. He has recently been unemployed and is waiting for a job in Shanghai. His family employs a young maid named A Jin from Wuxi, who is 18 years old. Although she is a village girl, she is somewhat attractive and dresses simply. Kan saw her and developed admiration for her. He joked with her in every possible way, hoping to fulfill his wishes. However, A Jin was pure and chaste and refused him sternly. Kan suffered from unrequited love and often muttered to himself, vowing to marry A Jin. If he could not achieve his goal, he would no longer live. He pestered the girl incessantly. After the girl told her master, Kan was reprimanded and not allowed to go out. Unexpectedly, he suddenly had a suicidal thought. He bought a package of raw opium and went to the girl's place, forcing her to commit suicide with him, hoping to be united in love in the afterlife. The girl snatched the opium from him and told her master, Wang Ji. Wang hated Kan for not repenting and fired him, giving him wages and travel expenses and telling him to go home quickly and find another job. After getting the money, he went out to prostitute and squander the money. After spending all the money, he thought that he had failed to win the girl's love and had lost his job. He had made a mess of things. He was not only ashamed to face people but also had no face to go home to see his brother and sister-in-law. He had the idea of committing suicide again. He pawned his clothes and bought one yuan of raw opium. At 9:30 p.m. on the 8th, he opened room number one at the Shunxing Inn at 402 Xujiahui Road. After smoking opium, he wrote several suicide notes at his desk (to Mr. and Mrs. Wang, Mr. and Mrs. Chen Zhuo, and the girl A Jin). As he was about to finish writing, at about 10 o'clock, the inn's tea waiter, Ni Xinghua (29 years old from Chongming), caught a glimpse of him and noticed that his appearance was unusual. He immediately asked him. Kan said, "I have taken poison and committed suicide. Please notify my master and tell him the address." The waiter rushed to report to his employer, Wang Ji. Then, Chen Zhuofu, the master of A Jin, rushed to the scene and took a car to Guangci Hospital. The poison recurred, and he was sent to the hospital for treatment, but it was ineffective. He died at 4 p.m. the next day. The hospital reported to the French police station, which sent detectives to investigate. Because there were no family members in Shanghai, the employer's representative, Mr. A, the witness Chen Zhuofu, Ni Xinghua, and the maid A Jin were summoned to the case yesterday and reported to the Second Special Court Procuratorate. Prosecutor Wang Ren, accompanied by a forensic doctor and a clerk, arrived at noon to examine the body. He sat on the public case and questioned the witnesses. The official announced that Kan Mengxiong had died of poisoning before his death. The body was photographed, embalmed, and buried by Tongren Fuyuan Tang, waiting for family members to claim it.

Taifeng Company Held a Shareholders' Meeting Yesterday to Discuss Reorganization and Resumption of Business. A Plan Was Proposed and Approved by 30 People on the Spot. 134

The Taifeng Canned Food Company on Nanjing Road is currently being liquidated by the court due to litigation. The company's shareholders, Deng Ruiji, etc., previously published an advertisement to convene a shareholders' meeting to discuss follow-up measures. Yesterday (the 10th) afternoon, a provisional general meeting of shareholders was held at the Dadong Restaurant. Shareholders who registered, including representatives, totaled more than 60 households. Deng Ruren chaired the meeting, reported on the progress of the situation, and proposed a settlement plan, which mainly included: (A) requesting creditors to stop accruing interest on external debts and repay the principal in installments, starting with 10%, totaling 60,000 yuan, and handing over the property of the Huaming Match Factory to the creditors. The company would redeem it within one year. Another 200,000 yuan of debt would be allocated, and the company would issue bonds to distribute to the creditors in exchange for compensation. If the creditors are willing to use the bonds as new shares, the company will accept them. The remaining debts will be repaid in ten years. (B) The company will be reorganized. Old shares will be converted at a ratio of three shares to one share, totaling 100,000 yuan. Another 100,000 yuan of new shares will be raised, and 100,000 yuan will be borrowed by mortgaging the assets, totaling 200,000 yuan in cash, which will be used as working capital and various expenses since the suspension of business. The chairman finally reported that the total number of shares represented at today's meeting was more than 1,400. Those who agree with this plan are requested to sign their names below. About 30 people signed on the spot. The shareholders then left the meeting one after another, and the meeting adjourned.

After a Female Bandit Was Arrested, Her Four Children Followed Her into Jail 135

All Young and No One to Adopt Them. The Female Bandit Wept Loudly in Court.

——Was She Fooled into Committing a Crime?——

Xue Sanzi from Funing opened a freight car company at 114 Guangfu Road, Zhabei, which was quite prosperous and had accumulated surplus capital, attracting the attention of bandits. At about 7 p.m. on May 8 of this year, three bandits suddenly broke in, each holding a pistol, and demanded 300 yuan in ransom. When they failed to obtain it, the bandits abducted Xue's beloved son, Da Shizi. Xue's wife, Xue Li, was greatly shocked and immediately reported to the police station, which sent police to search in all directions. Unexpectedly, Qin Longchi, a neighbor of Xue Sanzi, saw a bandit woman (Chen Wang) carrying Xue's child in her arms and sitting in a rickshaw on Gonghe Road. Her appearance was flustered, which made him very surprised. Knowing that the woman was not good, he stepped forward and grabbed the bandit woman. While they were arguing, Xue Li and others tracked them down and were overjoyed that their son was out of danger. The pearl was returned to Hepu. They called the police and sent the bandit woman, Chen Wang, to the Public Security Bureau and then to the local court for prosecution. She was charged with kidnapping and extortion. Yesterday morning at 10 o'clock, Judge Yang Liting opened the tenth courtroom for the trial. The plaintiff, Xue Li, filed a case, stated the previous situation, and requested prosecution. The judge ordered the detainee, Chen Wang (also known as Zhou Zhou), to be brought to the case for questioning. She was 36 years old, from Funing. Her husband, Zhou Fengxiang, worked in a yarn factory. Due to economic pressure, she was introduced by her fellow villagers Zhang Xiaosanzi and Liu Xiaoheshang to work as a wet nurse. She was also paid to wet nurse the Xue family's child for six yuan a month. She thought that they were all fellow villagers and did not suspect anything. She rashly followed Lu Xiaosanzi and others to the door of the Xue family on Guangfu Road. Zhang Xiaosanzi did not allow her to enter but ordered her to wait at the door. After a while, Zhang Xiaosanzi carried the Xue family's child out and told her to take the child back first, saying that he still had to go in and negotiate the price of the wet nursing. Unexpectedly, she was arrested on Gonghe Xin Road and accused of being a kidnapper. It was really a false accusation. She requested an investigation. Moreover, she had four children. Because no one was willing to adopt them, they were detained with her. After she finished her statement, she held her four children and cried non-stop. The oldest child was only eight years old, and the youngest was still in swaddling clothes. The innocent children also suffered the taste of prison and suffered with their mother. At this point, Prosecutor Lei Binzhang came to court to perform his duties and said that the defendant was caught on the spot and the victim had provided evidence. There was no way to deny the case. He requested a public trial. Finally, the appointed voluntary lawyer, Chen Kuitang, stood up to defend the defendant, saying that the defendant, Chen Wang, was still an ignorant rural woman who was fooled by others and mistakenly committed a crime. She had mitigating circumstances and requested a lenient sentence and a declaration of innocence. The judge considered it concluded and awaited the verdict. Chen Wang was returned to custody to await instructions.

The Late Chen Yide's Concubine Sues to Reclaim Her Son 136

Presents Photos as Proof; The Wife Firmly Denies

Chen Yipeizhen, a 31-year-old woman from Beiping currently residing at No. 2, Jiusi Lane, Xiangshi Road, French Concession, has hired a lawyer to file a lawsuit in the Civil Division of the Special District Court against Chen Zhou, the wife of the late Chen Yide. The suit seeks confirmation of parentage and a court order for the return of her son for upbringing. Ms. Chen claims that she had a relationship with Chen Yide, a wealthy real estate merchant from Suzhou residing at No. 260, Beile Road, in 1924. Because Chen was a Catholic and church rules forbade concubinage, he rented a house for her at No. 1024, Yongfu Lane, Avenue Edward VII, where they lived together. In July 1926, she gave birth to a son, nicknamed Xiong Guan, with the formal name Nengyi. The following year, due to Ms. Chen's poor health, Chen took the child back and entrusted him to his wife, Zhou, for upbringing. Zhou treated the child as if he were her own, born to her husband, showering him with love. Later, Chen passed away, and during the family dispute over the inheritance, Xiong Guan's existence helped to preserve the family assets. Recently, Ms. Chen has argued that her son, Xiong Guan, is growing up and should pursue his studies to become a good citizen. However, she claims that the wife, Zhou, pampers him excessively, using cars for transportation and living a life of luxury. She fears that this environment will turn him into a "high-class loafer." Therefore, she wants Zhou to return the child so she can raise him herself and enjoy the natural bond between mother and son. However, Zhou firmly denies that Xiong Guan is Ms. Chen's son, claiming he is her own biological child. This led to a breakdown in mediation, and Ms. Chen has formally filed a lawsuit, requesting a court decision. The court accepted the case, and yesterday morning at 11:00 AM, Judge Ma Yishu heard the case in Civil Courtroom No. 7. Both parties were present with their respective lawyers. The plaintiff, Chen Yipeizhen, stated, "I married Chen Yide in 1925. On July 21, 1926, I gave birth to Xiong Guan. In May of the following year, I fell ill, and Chen took the child to be raised by the defendant. Later, Chen passed away. When I went to their house, the defendant kept Xiong Guan because the family was dividing the inheritance. I often heard her falsely claiming that the child was born to me in October 1925 and that he is now ten years old. She (referring to the plaintiff) has never been to my house, and we barely know each other. Why is she suing now?" Ms. Chen replied, "The Chen family house has two stories. When I gave birth, there was obstetrician Hu Lezhen who can attest to it. Dr. Hu lives on North Sichuan Road. I was at my mother's home in Beiping for three years, which is why I am suing her now." The lawyer presented several photographs of Chen Yide, Ms. Chen, and the child as evidence. The judge asked the defendant if she recognized the people in the photos. Zhou replied, "The man is my husband. I don't know how he ended up taking pictures with another woman. I don't recognize the child in the photos."

Chinese Constable Accused by Mistress of Instigating Murder 137

Mistress Has Knife Wound on Chest; Police Will Conduct Detailed Investigation

Zhang Murui, a Chinese constable, No. 1191, from Shandong, at the Zhabei Police Station, was recently reported by his mistress, Yi Mei Yuan, along with her maternal uncle, Fang Jinxian, to the police for suspected instigation of murder. The police chief arrested Zhang and sent him to the First Special District Court yesterday morning, requesting detention. Qian Xunjiu, the police lawyer, presented the findings of the investigation, stating that on the morning of the 7th of this month, at 2:30 AM, a woman named Gong Meiyuan, residing at a certain number on Zhoushan Road, along with her maternal uncle, Fang Jinxian, reported to the police. The police noticed that the woman had a knife wound on her chest and sent her to Guangren Hospital for treatment. At the same time, they ordered Chinese Detective Zhu Shoulun and Western Detective Kai Nai Tai to investigate. According to Ms. Gong, on the morning of the 6th of this month, around 10:00 AM, while she was walking on Zhoushan Road, she suddenly encountered a stranger wearing a blue cloth short shirt and pants. The man told her that Constable No. 1191 had instructed him to tell her to go to the constable's house to collect money, and she could go there before 11:00 PM. Ms. Gong then went to the home of her maternal uncle, Fang Jinxian, at No. 470, Dapu Road, French Concession, and around 8:00 PM, she and Fang went to Zhang's house. While walking through the Chinese territory near the North Railway Station, they encountered the same man in the blue cloth shirt, who approached Ms. Gong and said that now was a good time to go and collect the money. He accompanied her, but when they reached Zhongxing Road, the man suddenly pulled out a knife and stabbed Ms. Gong in the chest, then dropped the knife and fled. Ms. Gong fell to the ground, injured, and was taken by Fang to the local Public Security Bureau, who then reported it to the Zhabei Police Station. Upon receiving the report, the detectives arrested Chinese Constable Zhang Murui, No. 291, at the police station. Zhang claimed that he met Gong Meiyuan around April 1930 and they began living together. In January of last year, the woman's mother and her sister came to Shanghai from their hometown and lived with them. He was responsible for all the daily expenses. However, in December, his mother also came to Shanghai from Shandong and naturally lived with them. Unexpectedly, Ms. Gong and her family objected and even broke his mother's bed, forcing her to sleep on the floor. Unable to tolerate this, he moved to No. 551, Zhoujiazui Road, and lived there with his mother. Gong often went to the Hongkou Police Station to make a scene. At that time, he was working at the Hongkou Police Station, and Chinese Deputy Chief Wen Youheng mediated the situation, ordering him to pay Gong 200 yuan in installments. To date, Chief Wen has transferred 140 yuan to Ms. Gong. However, Gong was extremely violent and continued to cause trouble at the police station. On April 29, the police took Gong to the court, but the judge reprimanded her and released her. The police accepted Zhang's request and transferred him to the Zhabei Police Station. Unexpectedly, Gong still frequently went to cause trouble, leading to this incident. He believes that Zhang was the mastermind. However, Zhang strongly denies instigating the attack. To clarify the facts, the police requested permission to detain him for further investigation. Judge Liu Yugui briefly questioned Zhang Murui and ordered his detention, postponing the hearing to a later date.
