Trolleybuses on Roads of the 17th and 18th Grades in the French Concession Temporarily Re-routed 139

The trolleybuses of the French Tramway Company, operating on the roads of the 17th and 18th grades from Xieqiao to the Great World, are being temporarily re-routed because the roads from Nanyang Bridge to Xieqiao are frequently damaged. The terrain is very low and the road surface is not solid, hindering the speed of the trolleybuses. The French Municipal Council has sent workers to raise the level of these roads, including Route Paul Beau, Rue du Marché, Xieqiao, and connecting roads such as Route Gustare de Galle, Avenue Hoche, Route Francis Garnier, Rue de la Porte Ouest, Avenue Joffre, Avenue de l'Observatoire, and Route Conty, by approximately one foot. Temporarily, the trolleybuses will be re-routed from Xieqiao via Boulevard de la Mission, to Route Francis Garnier, then east to Avenue Joffre, and north to the back gate of the Jingjiang Public Institute, connected to the French territory, then entering Nanyang Bridge iron gate, and continuing on the original route to the Great World. Once the repairs are completed, the trolleybuses will resume their original route.

Representatives of Two New Pharmaceutical Associations Travel to Beijing to Petition 141

Reportedly Resulting in Satisfaction

The Shanghai New Pharmaceutical Industry Association and the Pharmaceutical Factory Industry Association elected eight representatives, including Xu Xiaochu, Zhou Bangjun, Yuan Hesong, Xu Chao, Shen Jichuan, Tu Kunhua, Zhao Ruciao, and Sun Choucheng, to travel to Beijing to petition for the amendment of the regulations governing prepared medicines and pharmaceutical merchants. The representatives returned to Shanghai on the night train on the 9th. According to Sun Choucheng, they traveled to Beijing on the night train on the 6th and stayed at the Central Hotel. At 9:00 AM on the 7th, they went to the Ministry of Internal Affairs' Department of Health, where Director Jin Baoshan and Section Chief Zhou Wenda met with them for two and a half hours. That same noon, Administrative Yuan Secretary-General Chu Minyi hosted the representatives at the Public Recreation Club. Director Liu Ruiheng and Director Jin and Section Chief Zhou were also present. Director Liu promised to consider the association's submitted opinions and arranged to meet again the following morning. At 10:00 AM on the 8th, the representatives went to the department together. Director Liu stated that the representatives' opinions were indeed in support of the government and not intentionally evasive, and he agreed to handle them flexibly. He publicly explained the five points of flexible handling, which the representatives found satisfactory. They also requested to be present when the rules were amended to present their opinions in person. Director Liu also agreed to this. Director Jin then accompanied them on a tour of the various departments and to the Queen's Hotel for a banquet. That evening, the Nanjing New Pharmaceutical Association and Xinya, among others, hosted a banquet. The next day, when passing through Zhenjiang, representatives from the local New Pharmaceutical Association and Chinese and Western pharmacies sent representatives to accompany them on a tour of Jinshan, Jiaoshan, and Beigushan. They took a group photo in Boxian Park to commemorate the occasion.

Ministry of Communications Encourages Merchants to Use Telegrams for Debt Collection Because Transmission is Fast and Effective 143

To encourage merchants to use telegrams for debt collection, the Ministry of Communications has compiled five concise slogans: (1) Telegrams can prompt debtors to pay attention and prepare to clear debts early; (2) Telegrams for debt collection can be sent in advance without additional fees; (3) The amount of debt can be written in Arabic numerals to save on telegram fees; (4) If the recipient's name and address do not exceed fifteen characters, they will only be charged as five characters; (5) The procedures are simple, and the transmission is fast and effective. The slogans have been circulated to all telegraph offices nationwide to be stamped in scarlet on newspapers circulated among merchants to encourage them to try using telegrams.

The architecture is beautiful, and the scenery is serene, making it a unique hospital for treating lung diseases. For the past year, it has hired experts and purchased new equipment, with everything necessary available. Patients from near and far have flocked to the hospital. The original wards were insufficient to meet the demand, and latecomers often could not be accommodated. The hospital, recognizing the shortage, has been trying to expand. The ball organized by women leaders has promised to help as much as possible.

County Third District Cooperative Provides Agricultural Loans to Alleviate Farmers' Difficulties 146

The Xianqiao Credit Production and Sales Guarantee Cooperative in the Third District of Shanghai County, recognizing the decline of the rural economy and the farmers' urgent need for funds during planting season, is providing agricultural loans to alleviate their difficulties. The rules for these loans are as follows: (1) The purpose of the cooperative's credit department loans is to assist members in obtaining agricultural production funds, develop production enterprises, and other economically justifiable purposes. (2) Members applying for loans must first fill out an application form and submit it to the council for review to determine whether the use is normal, the repayment method is reliable, and the guarantee is reliable. (3) The cooperative's credit department loans are divided into three types: credit, guarantee, and mortgage. All are fixed-term loans. Borrowing societies must establish a loan agreement after their approval and assessment. (4) The guarantors of the cooperative's borrowing members are jointly responsible with the borrowers. The candidates are not limited to members, but must be approved by the cooperative, and the cooperative may notify them to be replaced at any time. (5) The collateral for the cooperative's borrowing members' mortgage loans is limited to movable property, immovable property, or readily salable items approved by the cooperative. (6) The funds borrowed by the cooperative's borrowing members are limited to agricultural production and agricultural side business funds. The term is limited to a maximum of five months. If the loan cannot be repaid on time, prior notice must be given, and the term may be extended, but not by more than two months. (7) If the borrowing member uses the borrowed funds for purposes other than those requested, the guarantor will be responsible for recovering them. (8) The interest rate on the cooperative's loans is 1.2% per month. (9) If there are any unaddressed matters in these rules, they will be amended by the cooperative affairs meeting. (10) These rules will be implemented upon approval by the members' congress.

Opening of the Nanshi Public Market 147

According to the Dayi News Agency, the open space on the bank of the Pu Zhao River, Xieqiao, Nanshi, has been vacant for nearly a year since the city government banned stalls. The stallholders have been extremely distressed, with nowhere to go. Xu Shushan and other leaders of the stallholders, deeply sympathetic to their situation, raised funds to lease a private open space in Shuangxingli, at the intersection of Xie Xu Road and Jumen Road, Nanshi, from the Sanyu Real Estate Company, to organize the "Shanghai Public New and Old Sundries Market" to allow the stallholders to concentrate their business. The preparations have been completed, and the market has been approved by the Public Security Bureau. The opening ceremony was held yesterday, attended by about 40 guests, including Zhang Sheng and Li Weixiong from the city party headquarters, and Wang Gang from the Social Affairs Bureau. It is reported that the market has hired Zhou Lianze as the chairman, Xu Shushan as the manager, Li Yunjie as the assistant manager, and Chen Baofeng as the field director, who are actively planning to improve business methods. The office is located at No. 1, Shuangxingli.

Reconstruction of the Waimalu Road in Wusong 148

The western section of Waimalu Road in Wusong has been in disrepair for a long time since the war. It is uneven, and the damage from shelling is still visible. The Municipal Bureau of Public Works has formally started the reconstruction, widening it to ten meters, and repaving the surface with asphalt and gravel. The Zhabei Water and Electricity Company is taking advantage of the road reconstruction to lay water pipes. The project is expected to be completed by the end of this month.

The Industry Association Reduces the Profit Margin on Coffins 149

The Shanghai Machinery Industry Association is one of the charitable organizations in Shanghai. It has always been dedicated to various charitable activities within its capabilities. The members of the association, recognizing the economic downturn and the social economic panic, and that there are many poor families in Shanghai, who are unable to afford coffins when faced with funerals, convened a committee meeting yesterday to reduce the profit margin on coffins from the 10th of this month (i.e., yesterday) to benefit poor families who have lost loved ones.

Salvaging the Sunken Asiafu Ship 150

The Asiafu ship, which sank in the Huangpu River near Lujiazui last winter after being struck by another vessel, has been the subject of a salvage plan by a Russian salvage company. They have completely pumped out the water that had accumulated inside the ship's hull. They have immersed four large iron barges into the river bed, and then encircled the bottom of the Asiafu ship with thin lead wires. They will then pump the water out of the barge compartments and use the buoyancy of the four barges to lift the Asiafu ship to the surface. It is reported that it is expected to be salvaged within three days.

Judgment in the Case Against Zhu Ziyun: The National Medical Association Proves the Prescription Was Not Inappropriate; The Court Found Zhu Ziyun Not Guilty Yesterday in Court 151

Zhu Ruiting, a clerk at the British American Tobacco Company from Wujiang, who lives at No. 2, Samsungli, Wansheng Bridge, Nanshi, recently hired lawyer Jiang Rong to file a criminal lawsuit in the First Special District Court of Shanghai against Zhu Ziyun, a Jiangwan pediatrician and traditional Chinese medicine doctor, for negligence in his practice that resulted in the tragic death of his five-year-old son, Binggen. The First Special District Court has concluded the trial, and details were recorded in this newspaper. Judge Feng Shide, who was presiding over the case, felt it necessary to send the prescription to the Shanghai National Medical Association for evaluation. He then announced the cancellation of the closing arguments and reopened the debate. The court has now received the evaluation report from the National Medical Association. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Feng continued the hearing in the Criminal Courtroom No. 2 and announced the National Medical Association's evaluation, stating that Zhu Ziyun's prescription was not inappropriate. The plaintiff's lawyer, Jiang Rong, immediately stated that the plaintiff had previously requested the court to send the case to the Central National Medical Museum for evaluation because, according to the plaintiff's knowledge, Zhu Ziyun had a special relationship with the National Medical Association. The plaintiff also received an anonymous letter from a Mr. Chen on Yong'an Street, also stating Zhu's relationship with the association. Now, the National Medical Association's evaluation only states that the herbs prescribed by Zhu Ziyun were indeed for the treatment of rubella, without any academic explanation. Therefore, the plaintiff fundamentally distrusts the evaluation. Furthermore, the plaintiff purchased the National Medical Encyclopedia, which, compared to Zhu Ziyun's prescription, shows that the herbs were entirely cooling, such as Xiaochuan Lian, mulberry leaves, and bamboo leaves, with very few diaphoretic herbs, which could cause the rubella to sink inward. The defendant's statements did not explain the source or nature of the herbs prescribed. Judge Feng stated that since the National Medical Association's evaluation could not be proven to be biased, there was no need for another evaluation. He then ordered the start of the arguments. The plaintiff's lawyer argued on academic facts, requesting that Zhu Ziyun be punished with the deserved punishment. Subsequently, lawyer Lu Qi argued on behalf of the defendant. There is no guarantee that every patient will survive. Now, Zhu Ziyun's prescription was not wrong. Traditional Chinese medicine cannot be interpreted out of context. The entire prescription must be explored together. The National Medical Association has evaluated Zhu's prescription and found that there was nothing inappropriate about it. The plaintiff alleged that Zhu Ziyun had a special relationship with the association. The defendant strongly denies this point. The plaintiff should bear the burden of proof and cannot make an empty argument. Furthermore, the National Medical Association's evaluation was a public decision made by all medical groups in Shanghai. Assuming that Zhu Ziyun had a considerable relationship with the National Medical Association and was biased, it would be impossible for him to have the power to have all the TCM doctors in the city protect him. Therefore, the plaintiff's argument is completely unfounded, and the defendant should be found not guilty. Judge Feng deliberated and announced the end of the arguments, finding Zhu Ziyun not guilty in court.

Fire in a Chicken and Duck Shop on the East Side of the Zilaihuo Street 155

At 11:40 PM the night before last, a fire broke out in a chicken and duck shop at No. 204, at the intersection of the East Zilaihuo Street in the French Concession's Caishi Street. The shop owner was upstairs and did not know how a fire started on the cotton quilt and clothes. Smoke and flames immediately filled the air, making it impossible to approach. Neighbors noticed and immediately ran to tell the patrolling constable, who reported it to the fire brigade. The fire brigade quickly arrived with a pumper and managed to extinguish the fire. Only the floorboards, walls, and stairs of the mezzanine were damaged, and the stairs were almost burned through. The second and third floors were full of tenants. If the fire had spread, the tenants upstairs would have had no way to escape. Fortunately, it did not spread. It is reported that the chicken and duck shop had fire insurance of several thousand taels. The police are thoroughly investigating the cause of the fire for verification.

Treating Life as a Game: Two Women Attempt Suicide in the Huangpu River and are Rescued: Neither Had Any Need to Commit Suicide, Seemingly Both are Mentally Ill 160

Around 11 o'clock yesterday morning, two young women attempted to throw themselves into the Huangpu River, but were unsuccessful. The reasons for their suicide attempts were: one felt ashamed for beating her husband, and the other was beaten by her husband. Coincidentally, both were quite loquacious. The details are as follows:

A Gui

Mao Zhongmao, a native of Ningbo, lives at No. 11, Dade Li, Yangshupu Road. He works at a factory in Longhua and is naturally timid. His wife, A Gui, is 25 years old, also from Ningbo, and is fiercely shrewish. When she roars like a lion, Mao dares not resist. However, Mao mostly resides at the factory. Recently, after returning home, he angered his wife for some reason. A Gui punched and kicked him, and then locked him in a room, depriving him of his freedom. A Gui, realizing her shame towards her husband, left alone, whereabouts unknown. Mao, released by a neighbor, waited two days for his wife to return and then sent a letter to his in-laws stating the situation to clear his name. Unexpectedly, A Gui went to the outside of the Xinguanshenmatou Wharf alone at 11 o'clock yesterday morning, intending to commit suicide by throwing herself into the Huangpu River. She hesitated before jumping. A Chinese constable from the West Sea Customs Water Police Station saw her and took her to the police station. She claimed that her husband disregarded her personal life, which led to her disillusionment with the world. The police station then ordered detective Li Wenzhu to investigate at the address. Neighbors stated that A Gui was fierce and abusive towards her husband, accusing her of feigning suicide to cover up her actions. The neighbors were told to wait for Mao to return home and then be brought to the police station for questioning.

Shu Ying

Zhang Shu Ying, a 22-year-old woman from Jiujiang, with a perm and fashionable attire, and a passable appearance, was married to her late husband. She remarried Jin Gaolong, a fellow native, and came to Shanghai with him, residing at No. 129, Minhou South Li, Hartung Road. Jin was originally a boatman, but is now unemployed. Recently, he accused his wife of infidelity and severely beat her, causing Shu Ying to be covered in bruises. Extremely resentful and disillusioned with the world, she went to the Xinguanshenmatou Wharf alone at 11 o'clock yesterday morning, boarded a sampan docked by Ah Hua, and pretended to cross to Pudong. When the boat reached the center of the river, she suddenly jumped to the bow, hoping to commit suicide by throwing herself into the Huangpu River. The sampan operator grabbed her and sent her to the Customs Water Police Station. When asked about the reason for her suicide attempt, Shu Ying, with tears in her eyes, took down her trousers, saying that her lower body was severely injured and requested an examination. The police station staff all saw her as a strange woman. Shu Ying then claimed that when she lived on the fifth floor of a building, her husband stabbed her right arm with a knife and falsely accused someone named Jia on the second floor of rape, intending to extort money. The matter was taken to the police station and sent to the Special District Court, where the man was imprisoned. She stated that the scar was still there. The police station dispatched detective Huang Songsheng to summon Jin Gaolong to the station. After the couple confronted each other, Shu Ying firmly refused to return with her husband. The police chief, unable to mediate the situation, decided to send her to the local court for a decision.

The Greater Shanghai Map is Scheduled for Publication 161

The Riyong Shenghuo She (Daily Life Society), located at the west end of Avenue Foch and Route Maier, announced in this year's "Life Quick View" that the newly revised Greater Shanghai Map was originally scheduled for publication in mid-May. Letter to the Editor 172

Dear Editor, I have recently read a news report in your newspaper on the 7th of this month entitled "Fighting over Passengers, Disregarding Knives." The report stated that Yu Qi, a Cantonese man working as a host at the New Asia Hotel on North Sichuan Road, and his fellow native Chen Huaye, started a fight over passengers and injured people. It was reported that a passenger named Yu Jinhe, who recently arrived in Shanghai from Guangdong, was staying in room 403. According to the hotel's custom, guests who are new to Shanghai and unfamiliar with the area are to be accompanied by a host to various places for sightseeing. This is astonishing. After investigating, our hotel does not have an employee named Yu Qi or Chen Huaye. According to the police records, Yu and Chen also stated that they had no occupation. Furthermore, our hotel has no custom of having a host accompany guests for sightseeing. The guest staying in room 403 is also not named Yu Jinhe. It is believed that the report is inaccurate. Therefore, I am writing to your newspaper to request that you verify the facts and make a correction. Sincerely, The New Asia Hotel, June 10

Reader Submission: Chinese People Urgently Need to Change Their Mentality 173

— Liang

The Chinese people have long held a superstitious mentality towards foreign businesses. Even in the financial sector, the general public views foreign banks as the most trustworthy, while often neglecting or even intentionally criticizing domestic banks. The reason given is that foreigners have excellent credit, and foreign banks have substantial and reliable capital. For decades, this mentality has been deeply rooted in the minds of the Chinese people and is difficult to change.

But what is the credit of foreign banks really like? Let's briefly examine the facts over the years. In the past decade or so, many foreign banks have gone bankrupt or suspended operations: (1) Shanghai Guangxing Bank, established by American businessmen in 1919, was closed and liquidated in 1922 due to poor business performance and the impact of the failure of the Eastern Grand Bank. (2) Zhihua Bank, established in 1918 by the American Insurance Trust Company, Commercial Bank, San Francisco National Bank, and Chicago Continental Bank, was closed in 1924 due to losses from gold trading. (3) Datong Bank, a Sino-Japanese joint venture, suspended operations in 1927 due to heavy withdrawals during political unrest, as related banks refused to provide assistance. (4) The Sino-French Industrial Bank, established in 1912 with its headquarters in Paris and branches in Shanghai, Beijing, Tianjin, Hankou, Yunnan, Guangzhou, Shantou, and Fengtian, had the right to issue currency in China but suspended operations in the second half of 1921 due to poor business management. (5) The Sino-Russian Daosheng Bank was initially backed by the Russian government, but its business was severely affected after Russia's defeat in the Russo-Japanese War, and its branches in China were closed. (6) The Sino-Japanese Joint Venture Bank of China, with a branch in Shanghai, closed in the winter of 1928 due to runs in Tianjin and international political relations. (7) The China-American Maoye Bank, a Sino-American joint venture with its headquarters in Beijing and a branch in Shanghai, collapsed due to poor business management. Most recently, the American Merchant Meifeng Bank suddenly announced its closure. All of these banks, whether foreign-owned or Sino-foreign joint ventures, have gone bankrupt, proving that creditworthiness is what makes a bank successful, regardless of its origins.

Meifeng Bank had been in business for twenty years, with a capital of US$550,000 and Chinese currency $1,250,000, a public reserve of over Chinese currency $2 million, and total assets and liabilities of approximately $20 million. It was considered a mid-to-upper-level foreign bank, and the Chinese people had great faith in it. In 1932, its deposits totaled over 10,330,000 yuan, and recent reports indicate that they were between 8 and 9 million yuan. Depositors came from forty countries, with Russian and American depositors being the most numerous, but we estimate that Chinese deposits in the bank were very substantial.

Foreign banks take advantage of the consular jurisdiction granted by unequal treaties and are not subject to Chinese law. Many of those that go bankrupt are never properly liquidated, and only a few are fully liquidated. The best outcome is usually a long-term payment with non-interest-bearing bonds. The Chinese people suffer greatly from this, but cannot complain. Even if a foreign bank is truly substantial and reliable, it will only fully utilize Chinese deposits to engage in various speculative activities. Meifeng was affected by its own country's silver policy, which caused land prices to plummet, exchange rates to fall sharply, and speculation in American stocks. Its reserves were depleted, leading to a standstill. The dangers of its business were evident, yet the Chinese people ignored this and remained blindly superstitious. This is truly lamentable.

From now on, the Chinese people should learn from the closure of Meifeng Bank and fundamentally break the superstitious mentality towards foreigners. They should focus on domestic banks and deeply trust them. As the saying goes, it is never too late to mend the fold after the sheep have been lost. It is not too late for us to change our mentality. In fact, many domestic banks are well-funded and have excellent credit. Only a few small banks that are not members of the industry association are slightly inferior. As for the issuance of convertible notes, in terms of reserve requirements, Chinese banks hold 60% in cash and 40% in securities, or even more than 60% in cash. Foreign banks use different reserve ratios, such as 2:1, 3:1, or 40%, but all are lower than the ratio set by our country. There is no doubt about this.

Moreover, the government is making every effort to regulate and improve the financial system. Although the market is sluggish, the future holds much promise. In short, our gaze should be based on facts. For the sake of the individual and the nation, we must trust Chinese banks.

Spring and Autumn

Tidbits 174

— (Zui Qiao)

I often see opium addicts gather up all the dross from their opium lamps, to burn for another hit; they also lick all traces from their trays. Not a single bit of waste! If we young people could be as frugal with our time and money, not wasting a bit, then that would be great! When we are sitting in a vehicle, the road ahead seems to be still, unmoving. But when we turn to look at the road behind us, it rushes by like water. This is a clear indication that "the road forward requires effort and gradual progress to reach the goal! But if you retreat, then it will be very fast indeed.”

Speaking of money, everyone curses it, especially those of us who are poor. But it is an ignorant and stupid thing. All the evil and all the power are created by human folly. If we have enough money, then we will forget ourselves and use the money to dominate the weak!

A Visitor from Jinan Speaks 175

— Qiu Niang

A colleague, Mr. Ma, has returned from Jinan and told me about the recent situation there. I have recorded it as follows:

Jinan is the location of the Shandong provincial government. All civil servants, under the direction of Chairman Han Fuju, must wear black uniforms and hats when going to and from work. Recently, a weekly meeting is held every Monday at the large parade ground outside Jinan city, about seven or eight Chinese miles from the city. The meeting is scheduled for 5:00 AM. Those coming from the city are not allowed to travel by carriage or horse. Chairman Han also leads by example and walks there around 4:00 AM. At 5:00 AM sharp, he personally calls the roll, and no one dares to be absent. Those who are a few minutes late will be sent back to their original county governments by the headquarters to be taken care of and await punishment.

Those who serve the provincial government, except for those who have family members who can freely rent houses outside, must live in dormitories. It is said that the provincial government dormitories are very large, but there is only one toilet, and it is far from the dormitories. During the cold winter months, even to urinate or defecate is a difficult trek. Therefore, some people have adopted a chamber pot policy to overcome this difficulty. When Chairman Han discovered this, he imposed a one-month salary reduction for "laziness." Since then, the chamber pot policy has been shut down, and some people have promoted the use of spittoons instead of chamber pots, but the results have been the same and they have been punished.

All civil servants in Jinan wear homespun clothing, which is very plain. It is said that a civil servant wore woven woolen shoes to work and was seen by Chairman Han. Chairman Han immediately saluted him. The civil servant was at a loss and did not know what to do. Han said, "I am not saluting you, I am saluting your beautiful shoes." The civil servant immediately took off his shoes on the spot. Sadly, a pair of socks was sacrificed.

The weather in Jinan in late spring is still cold, so many people still wear heavy cotton-padded coats and trousers. This is very different from the areas south of the Yangtze River, where it is too hot to wear a lined jacket.

Philosophy of Drinking 176

— 19

One can discern a person's character through their drinking habits. People tend to be reserved and restrained in ordinary circumstances. This restraint is to preserve one's face, so their demeanor is often unnatural. However, after three cups of yellow wine, one unconsciously speaks without reservation and acts without constraint. Therefore, to observe a person, one should observe them while drinking.

A person dressed in coarse cloth, wearing straw sandals, standing at the entrance of a wine shop, digging out a few copper coins to exchange for a cup of white liquor, drinking it all in one gulp, and then covering their nose and mouth with their hand, unwilling to let even a trace of the alcohol escape, is someone who rarely drinks; hence, they cherish it greatly. Their purpose in drinking is not for enjoyment, but to dispel the cold or to invigorate themselves, so that they can continue to toil like beasts of burden.

Three or four friends stroll into a tavern, order dishes before even drinking. They engage in finger-guessing games, faces red and veins bulging, voices shaking the surroundings; moreover, they are unwilling to yield to each other, as if they have deep-seated hatred. If, by accident, a wine pot is overturned, they do not regret it much, and simply order another. These friends do not know how to drink. If even decades-old vintage wines are consumed in this way, onlookers would truly feel sorry for those fine wines. People who drink like this are probably fond of activity and not fond of stillness.

One or two close friends sit facing each other at a table. The dishes do not need to be exquisite, but good wine must be consumed. They sip gently, engage in quiet conversation, and stop drinking when they have had enough, not adding more wine. These friends truly know how to drink; their character is rarely muddled, or their temper has already completely subsided.

As for those who go mad after drinking, some prefer gentle persuasion, while others prefer harsh persuasion; from this, one can also discern a person's character.

— Juan Yin

Records of the Imperial Fragrance, Misty and Vague 178

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

"Remember! We must all be extremely careful today." Eight people exhorted each other: "No matter what, don't do anything to offend the Empress Dowager; as long as we can always show a smile, and respectfully obey orders, then today will surely be happy from beginning to end, and perhaps her smile will thus be able to extend for a few more days."

These words were naturally welcomed by everyone, and they carefully returned to their designated duties.

Kunming Lake is a famous scenic spot in the Summer Palace. Although it is man-made, it is quite wide enough for the Empress Dowager to travel back and forth in her yacht. Regarding the Empress Dowager's yacht, the author has already mentioned it in Chapter 13; but to preserve the old system of the palace, we may as well still call it the "Imperial Boat." The Imperial Boat does not often appear on Kunming Lake, because the Empress Dowager is not as free as Grandmother Jia in "Dream of the Red Chamber." Only in a period after late spring and before early autumn can she slightly enjoy the pleasure of touring the lake: so today's outing can truly be considered a rare event.

The style of the "Imperial Boat" is very ordinary, just a large boat with a canopy, using oars and bamboo poles as tools for sailing; in the middle, there is also a cabin, but it is built particularly tall, and carved exquisitely, with vermilion lacquer shining brightly, having the same gorgeousness as those palaces on the shore. Therefore, it is not wrong for me to call it a "floating palace on the lake!" (336)

Floating Palace on the Lake 179

East Big Pond in Wuxi 180

— (Shu Fan)

On the south side of Mount Xi, there is a spring called White Sand. The local gazetteer records: it does not dry up even in severe droughts and irrigates thousands of acres of fields. Below it is a large pool, with water even darker and deeper, which the locals call the East Big Pond. It is secluded and deeply hidden, rarely visited by tourists. This month, on a certain Sunday, I returned from the Two Caves in Yixing and passed by Meiyuan. My servant told me about it, so I ventured into it. The pond is more than two li away from the road, and can be reached on foot; at first glance, it doesn't seem very special, but after exploring it thoroughly, one realizes its extraordinary nature. Walking along the eastern cliff of the pond, passing "Peach Blossom Spring," the ancient pines are transformed into dragons, appearing to seize people; looking across the bank, the dense shade obscures the setting sun, and the faint sunlight leaks through like golden threads, like green hair; entering the pond, the fish stir up the waves, and from time to time create water flowers that fly onto the treetops and into one's sleeves; there are also crows cawing urgently, a scene that even the most skilled artist would find difficult to depict. To the north, Mount Hui forms a barrier, deep and solemn, like a large encircling screen. Extending westward, it becomes a lush forest, stretching for three or four li, the East Pond like a half-ring of green grave jade, a clear atmosphere overflowing, with pine resin and bamboo powder intermingling. Circulating around the pond, opening up a secluded space, one cannot but fully appreciate its charm. A square pond, half a mirror, and yet so much contained within, it is truly extraordinary!

Places Visited

Scenic Spots of Southern Zhao 181

— Lifang

In the pleasant fourth month, the weather is neither cold nor warm, it is truly the season for travel. I, along with Lu and Ye, embarked on a boat, drifting on the Zhao Creek. Originally, we intended to go to Cloud Nest, but the north wind was blowing strongly, and the boatman didn't have the strength to row the boat to Cloud Nest in one day. Amidst the sounds of oars, before we knew it, the moon was rising at dusk, and we docked at Digang for the night.

The next morning, we took a walk ashore, and Lu Ye led me into the scenic spots of Southern Zhao.

This place is not a Buddhist palace, nor is it a hermit's abode. Instead, it is a spirit writing altar dedicated to Lu Zu, presided over by ordinary people. Although they seem to be establishing teachings like a religious order, they also somewhat resemble a gathering place for scholars and students to cultivate themselves. According to the inscription on the stele erected inside: this place is called Yunyi Hall, founded during the Qianlong and Jiaqing periods of the Qing Dynasty. Their undertakings are all in the realm of charity, such as releasing animals, cherishing written words, providing medical care, dispensing medicine, running charitable schools, as well as prolonging life and delivering the dead, which is close to the era of divine power. The words "Scenic Spots of Southern Zhao" are the four large characters on the wall in front of the gate, which have not encountered the disasters of war. There is a story passed down about this place, which Lu Ye told me, and it goes like this:

At that time, when the troubles of war arose, the disciples in this Yunyi Hall all went to ask Lu Zu. The spirit writing pen came down, but it said, "The scenic spots of Southern Zhao are unharmed." Therefore, the people of Digang all took refuge here, but unexpectedly, they were all burned to ashes. After the rebellion was quelled, only the four characters "Scenic Spots of Southern Zhao" remained, and all the other buildings were reduced to ashes. Perhaps that was the wonderful writing of the spirit writing friends, let's not mention that for now.

We came to sightsee, so we naturally couldn't ignore the task of collecting local customs and habits. We only felt that the scenic spots of Southern Zhao are truly the scenic spots of Southern Zhao.

After entering the gate, there is a courtyard of flowers and trees. In the middle is a large fish pond, across which spans a stone bridge resembling a long rainbow. Around it are neat stone railings. Dozens of golden carp are kept in the pond. Leaning against the railings and watching them, one experiences the joy of Zhuangzi on the Hao River. This charm is no less than that of the Jade Spring on the lake. On both sides are rows of open halls, with courtyards such as Ode to Wine Studio and Tung Tree Shade Retreat. If one had the opportunity to study here throughout the four seasons, one would truly have the feeling of enjoying studying, how wonderful!

Yunyi Hall is built facing the pond. Going in from here, there are winding corridors, creating an engaging atmosphere. In the backyard, there are even more randomly stacked artificial mountains. On one side, ancient trees reach the sky, and on the other side, famous flowers are planted in profusion. At the end of the corridor, there is a four-sided hall, which also has a garden-like flavor. Unfortunately, it seems that it has not been repaired for a long time, so the weeds have grown over one's ankles.

There are also many calligraphic works by famous people here, such as Liang Shanzhou, Zhu Shijun, and Peng Yulin, all with their own touch. The elegance of the names of all the courtyards is rarely seen elsewhere. For example, the "Play and Enjoy Admonition" written by Liang Shanzhou, and the place for offering sacrifices to Kui Xing, named "Reading Place," it is truly ingenious and skillfully obtained.

In a hurried glance, we strolled around this small town, only to see a stream of water encircling the small market town in the middle. The secluded streets and alleys were quiet, with no one coming or going, making us worldly people feel refreshed. This small market town is also the scenic spots of Southern Zhao!

The Fifth Standing Committee Meeting of the National Games Preparatory Committee 182

Passed the Work Plan of the Venue Equipment Division; Overseas Chinese in Vietnam Request to Participate in Cycling Competition

The Fifth Standing Committee Meeting of the National Games Preparatory Committee was held at 10:00 AM the other day in the Municipal Government Conference Room. The details are as follows:

Committee Members Present: Wu Tiecheng, Chu Minyi (Hao Dai), Wang Shijie (Hao Dai), Pan Gongzhan, Cai Jinjun (Yi Baoshou Dai), Wang Rutang (Liu Yunfang Dai), Hao Gengsheng, Lei Zhen (Hao Dai), Xu Peihuang, Shen Siliang, Cai Zengji; Attendees: Jiang Xiangqing, Wu Bangwei, Shao Rugan, Ma Chonggan; Chairman: Wu Tiecheng (Pan Gongzhan Dai); Recorder: Wang Daxu

(2) Committee Member Wang Zhengting sent a letter requesting approval for overseas Chinese in Vietnam to participate in the cycling competition of the Games, or for individual performances based on a letter from Tan Meiguan. The committee may then approve it, providing only food and lodging, but not covering travel expenses. (3) The Work Plan of the Venue Equipment Division of the Committee. Resolution: Except for the various sports fields, which will be decided based on the amount of funding available, the rest is approved. (4) The Education Department of Zhejiang Province sent a letter inquiring whether personnel serving outside the province can represent the province in various competitions of the National Games. Resolution: Respond that Article 30 of the Games Competition Regulations stipulates that representing the unit where one is currently located refers to the place where one is currently serving, and it is not appropriate to represent one's province of origin in the competition. (5) How should the funds needed for the committee's preparation be allocated? Resolution: Immediately divide the 70,000 yuan check to Minister Wang of the Ministry of Education and Minister Kong of the Ministry of Finance, and send a letter to the Municipal Government requesting that it first allocate 50,000 yuan to repay advances and to quickly repair the venue. (6) Draft regulations for the Shanghai Municipal Public Utilities Bureau to bid for advertising inside and outside the sports field. Resolution: Approved.

Two New World Records in the Men's and Women's 100 Meters 187

Japan's Yoshioka - 10.3 seconds; America's Stephens - 11.6 seconds

Female

(Reuters, Kansas City, 9th) American Ms. Stephens today achieved a new world record of 11.6 seconds in the women's 100 meters, surpassing Ms. Stanislava Walasiewicz's world record of 11.8 seconds by one-tenth of a second. On May 5, Ms. Stephens set a new world record of 5.9 seconds in the women's 50 meters, breaking the old record of 6.4 seconds jointly held by Ms. Mayer of Czechoslovakia and Ms. Waller of Poland.

Male

(Japanese United News Agency, Tokyo, 10th) When Japanese and Filipino athletes held a track and field competition at the Koshien Stadium in Osaka on the 9th, Japanese athlete Yoshioka Ryutoku ran the 100 meters in 10.3 seconds, setting a new world record. The previous world record of 10.3 seconds was held by three athletes: Canadian William, American Doolan, and Mitogav. Yoshioka painstakingly studied the running method in the second half of the 100 meters and vigorously practiced it. As a result, he increased his speed in the second half of the race and achieved this result. The Japanese Track and Field Federation plans to officially recognize this record and include it in the world record table.

The Shanghai Chinese Tennis Federation's Fifth Xianfang Cup League, which has been preparing for some time, closed its registration yesterday. A total of ten teams participated. The details are listed below.

Zhejiang Education Department Order: Submit Reports on Property Increases and Decreases 195

The Zhejiang Education Department ordered all educational institutions: It has been found that all educational institutions in the province should have prepared and submitted property catalogs at the end of last year, as stipulated by the Education Department. The department has previously issued a notice to comply with this requirement. Now that the 23rd year is also coming to an end, the Education Department specifically ordered on the 9th that all institutions that have previously submitted property catalogs in the 21st year should immediately submit one copy each of the property increase report and the property decrease report for the 22nd and 23rd years. Starting from July of the 24th year, one copy each of the monthly increase report or decrease report must be prepared and submitted together with the expenditure calculation report. Those who have not yet prepared and submitted a property catalog in the 21st year should start preparing one immediately and submit it to the department, including all original properties and items purchased before June of the 24th year. Starting from July of the 24th year, one copy each of the monthly increase report and decrease report should be prepared and submitted together with the expenditure calculation report. The property catalog should be prepared in accordance with the "Simple Explanation of Property Compilation Procedures," and the property increase report and property decrease report should be prepared in accordance with the "Instructions for Filling out Property Increase Reports and Property Decrease Reports" to ensure uniformity and facilitate auditing. The reports should be prepared and submitted to the department before July 15th without delay.

End of Semester: Universities Prepare for Large Number of Graduates to Study Abroad 198

Global Student Association Prepares Farewell Party

As the 23rd year is coming to an end, a large number of graduates from universities in the country are preparing to study abroad. The Global Student Association in this city will hold a farewell party in the middle of next month. The details are as follows:

Large Number of Students Preparing to Study Abroad

The summer vacation is approaching, and the semester is coming to an end. Graduates from public and private colleges and universities in the country are preparing to study abroad. The Global Chinese Student Association in this city has recently been busy handling procedures for studying abroad. According to Wu Deyin, director of the association's travel and reception department, due to the sharp decline in the U.S. dollar this year, the number of students going to the United States has increased compared to the past. It is estimated that there will be more than 200 students going to the United States this year. Although the number of students going to Japan has been restricted by the Ministry of Education's preliminary funding plans, most have not followed the Ministry's instructions. Therefore, the number of students going to Japan this year is still considerable.

Procedures for Applying for Study Abroad Certificates

Many students are unclear about the procedures for applying for study abroad certificates from the Ministry of Education. The Global Student Association will issue the following statement: When applying for a study abroad certificate from the Ministry of Education, the following documents are required for those going to Japan: diploma (graduates of colleges and universities are qualified), two photos, certificate stamp fee of three yuan, guarantee letter, and bank or institution deposit certificate. For those going to Europe and the United States, the required documents are the same as for Japan, except that there is no need to submit a deposit certificate. For those who are unclear about the procedures for applying for a passport, inquiries can be made to the association, and a response will be provided the next day.

Farewell Party to be Held Next Month

The Global Student Association and various institutions and schools hold a farewell party for students studying abroad every year. In addition to the social gathering, famous people are invited to give speeches and provide various guidance for studying abroad, which is very beneficial. This has been done more than a dozen times with great success. This year's farewell party will be held in the middle of next month. The association will send letters to various educational and cultural institutions and school organizations in the city to jointly initiate and be responsible for the preparations. It is expected that the event will be a grand occasion.

National Language Association Assists in Promoting Suzhou Phonetic Symbols 203

Methods Have Been Determined by the Dialect Committee, and a Joint Promotion Committee Will Be Organized

The National Mandarin Education Promotion Association recently held a dialect committee meeting to discuss and decide to assist the Preparatory Committee for Mandarin Unification of the Ministry of Education in promoting Suzhou phonetic symbols. The details are as follows:

Motivation for Promotion

The Preparatory Committee for Mandarin Unification of the Ministry of Education commissioned Guo Luji, who arrived in Ping from Tianjin on March 1st, to discuss the promotion of Suzhou phonetic symbols with Li Jinxi, Qian Xuantong, Wang Yi, and Chen Songping, standing committee members of the committee, to help the public become literate. They held several meetings in Beixiaozhonghai, revised the Suzhou phonetic symbol table, and decided to print 30,000 copies for dissemination and promotion. Guo Luji was also publicly recommended to go to Suzhou and cooperate with the education authorities to promote the use of phonetic symbols in accordance with the Ministry of Education's order in the 19th year, in order to help the public become literate.

Suzhou Phonetic Symbols

The Suzhou phonetic symbols were determined by Wu Zhihui and Chen Songping in the 8th year of the Republic and published on a large sheet. They were revised by Zhao Yuanren in the 19th year and compiled into a general table of phonetic symbols. This time, they have been revised again, with a total of 33 initials, 21 finals, and 17 combined finals, totaling 81. The symbol style is mainly designed to be convenient for the public, easy to recognize and remember. It is said that the new table of 30,000 copies has been printed by the Mandarin Unification Association and will soon be transported to Suzhou for application.

Compilation and Printing of Books and Newspapers

Committee member Guo Luji, based on the revised Suzhou phonetic symbol table, collected more than 4,000 commonly used Suzhou characters and compiled a "Suzhou Homophone Character Table." He also compiled a "Suzhou Phonetic Symbol Textbook" and a "Suzhou Phonetic Symbol Writing Template." He has also recently compiled a set of "Suzhou Phonetic Symbol Supplementary Books." All the books have been completed and sent to Shanghai for printing. It is expected that they will be published in mid-May. The printing costs are being donated by dozens of people, including Zhang Zhongren, Wu Zhihui, Qian Xinru, Chen Gongliang, and Tu Peicheng.

Assisting in Promotion

The National Mandarin Education Promotion Association resolved at the National Mandarin Education Conference in the 20th year of the Republic to compile phonetic symbols for various dialects and organize a dialect committee for research and discussion. The association recently convened a meeting of the dialect committee to discuss and decide to assist the Preparatory Committee for Mandarin Unification of the Ministry of Education in promoting Suzhou phonetic symbols, and appointed members to join the committee member Guo from the Unification Association, and Suzhou party and government personnel, and enthusiastic people to organize the Suzhou Phonetic Symbol Promotion Committee to preside over the dissemination and promotion.

Securities: Fall Quickly, Rise Quickly; Public Bonds Unexpectedly Rebound; Salt Tax Rises and Halts 209

All Bonds Rise by About Two Yuan; Rumors of Benefits for 96 Abound

Yesterday, the Shanghai Chinese Merchant Securities Exchange saw a favorable turn in the situation in Hebei, with the possibility of a peaceful resolution improving the atmosphere. The entire short-selling front shook, with retail investors rushing to cover their positions and large investors turning from short to long. The upward trend was strong, and all bonds rose in unison. Salt tax bonds and treasury bonds even surged by four yuan and halted trading, contrasting sharply with the sharp drop and halt at the end of last week. The volatility was so wild and sudden that it made operators lose their composure. Trading was extremely active, with a total turnover of more than 40 million yuan in the morning and afternoon sessions, truly a rare and grand occasion for the public bond market. The trend and future are temporarily expected to have another twist and turn. The market for the 96 public bond rose even more sharply yesterday and was unstoppable, because large short positions had been covered, the short side suddenly appeared weak, and the strength of the long side suddenly increased. In addition, the stimulus of a certain rumor favorable to the long side made the rise even more fierce. In the morning session, the near-term rose by 6.5 jiao and the far-term rose by more than one yuan. At the close, the near-term surged by one yuan, and the far-term did not continue to rise due to selling by the long side, and the market price was inverted. The market may recover slightly today. Yesterday's market price results showed a uniform surge of more than one yuan to a huge four yuan. There were large orders from the 4th, 21st, 48th, and 44th brokers, and most of the selling orders were scattered. The comparison table of the highest and lowest results is listed on the left.

Yarn and Cotton: Short Covering and Long Positions Rise Simultaneously; Yarn Prices Recover by More Than Two Yuan 211

Local Sichuan Merchants Suddenly Increase Purchases

After a sharp decline in the yarn market the previous day, the market rebounded and rose today, and the situation is firm. This is due to the fact that the continuous decline has been too great. The current situation has eased, people's hearts have turned, the wind of speculation has suddenly risen, short positions have been closed, long positions have been increased, and both sides have driven side by side, so the market has risen.

Jinji Runkang Covers Large Short Positions

In the pre-market trading of standard yarn, the near-month was still determined to be firmer than the far-month, and buyers were active. The atmosphere in the second and third sessions suddenly tightened. Due to the rise and halt of public bonds, Runkang covered a large number of short positions, and long positions also increased. Both sides drove side by side, so the rebound became stronger. As a result, each month rose by 1.4 jiao to 2 yuan compared with the closing price of the previous day. The afternoon session opened slightly lower, and the table was flat and tired, and the shape was calm. The trading became tight after the second and third sessions, because Runkang continued to cover short positions. The near-month closed sharply higher, and the Sichuan merchants' spot purchases were smoother and rose higher, but the far-month was normal. As a result, the near-month rose by another 3.4 jiao compared to the morning closing price, and the far-month rose by 1.2 jiao. High Expectations for American Cotton; Cotton Market Shows Significant Improvement 212

After a sharp decline, the cotton market has rebounded rapidly. This is primarily due to positive news regarding peace and a rebound in the yarn market, which has boosted confidence. American cotton prices are rising, with floating positions being covered. However, foreign merchants are still selling on the rallies. Local cotton stocks remain ample, and factories are suspending operations, with little hope of a return to normal, as the demand for raw materials has decreased.

Special Trading Session Sees Gains Across May and June

In the pre-market session, all months rose uniformly, displaying a sharp upward trend. This was largely due to the intensity of the rebound following consecutive days of decline. Foreign merchants continued to sell, with the distant months slightly lower at the close. Ultimately, all months closed up four to five and a half jiao compared to the previous day’s close. The market was relatively flat in the afternoon session, with all months falling by one to one and a half jiao. However, the second and third auctions were slightly higher. The market tightened sharply at the close due to positive news regarding American cotton prices, supporting the market. However, the distant months saw a decline of five fen in the auction. As a result, all months closed up five fen to 1.2 jiao compared to the morning close. The following sales were recorded: Geng Feng 2,000 dan, Tong Ji 4,220 dan, Ji Feng 3,100 dan, He Xing 5,500 dan, Tai Yu 2,100 dan, Shen Chang 3,800 dan (partially), Rui Da 5,000 dan, Shen Ji 17,200 dan, Xin Cheng 1,300 dan, Yi Feng 5,500 dan, Chang Yu 3,600 dan, and Da Chang 1,900 dan. Grains: Flour and Wheat Recover Rapidly in Unison 214

The flour market rebounded sharply after opening this morning. The shoreline wheat quotation was about two to three jiao better than Chicago's. Canadian wheat was unchanged. The prior week's decline was deemed excessive. Tianjin has recently turned slightly more active. According to the consolidated price there, it is already close to reasonable (currently selling at 4.5 jiao). Therefore, these merchants are buying the near-term contracts, immediately stirring up excitement. For the deferred contracts, inland merchants' intentions are also good. They are progressing smoothly. At the closing, the near-term contracts were up three to four fen, and the deferred contracts were up two to three fen. When the market opened in the afternoon, initial rain showers softened sentiment slightly. However, renewed bidding by the Tianjin merchants reinvigorated the near-term contracts. Deferred contracts continued to improve due to short covering by inland merchants and local traders. It is believed that further development will depend on flour sales for stability. As a result, this month’s contract surged 5.25 fen, July’s contract rose five fen, August’s contract rose four fen, September’s contract rose three fen, October’s contract rose 2.75 fen, and November’s contract rose 1.5 fen.

When wheat was priced, anxiety rose in both local and foreign quarters after a long spell of dry weather in various locations. Inland merchants also raised rice prices and took a uniformly bullish stance. Therefore, after the opening, bids for all months were brisk, with transactions active, resulting in a rebound of eight fen to one jiao. When the market opened in the afternoon, sentiment was greatly relieved by the rain. The July contract briefly fell five to six fen, down to 3.1 jiao. The near-term contracts also eased by three to nine fen simultaneously. Later, inland merchants' intentions turned very positive, rebounding three to four fen. Future ups and downs will depend on flour sales. As a result, the July contract rose nine fen, and the August, September, and October contracts rose eight fen. The spot wheat market remains stable, with arrivals peaking, reaching over 10,000 bags in the past two days. Dealers have not turned greedy, making it difficult to raise prices. The opening price was 3.42 yuan for wheat from Lin Huai Guan, Sha He Ji, Guan Dian, and Taizhou, 3.33 yuan for wheat from Jiang Yan, and 3.30 yuan for wheat from Taiping Fu, Yangzhou, and Hezhou, with Xin Da shipping out 2,000 bags and Shen Da shipping out 1,500 bags, it is said.

In Shanghai's northern ports, fourteen or fifteen boats arrived from various routes along the river yesterday. The market is showing a good appetite for various types of rice. Oil Market: Hankou Crude Tung Oil Prices Fall 220

After crude tung oil in Hankou rose to 44 yuan per barrel, it increased by another 4 jiao. Although foreign firms continue to purchase, they believe that the price is too high and must be suppressed. Therefore, all foreign firms are refraining from purchasing at high prices. The market has inevitably suffered a setback. According to last night's Hankou dispatch, prices have fallen to 42.6 yuan, a decrease of 2 yuan. This is a natural correction after the large price increase. However, foreign firms still have strong demand, and production area inventories are dwindling. The source of Hankou is becoming increasingly scarce. Even if temporarily suppressed, the overall trend is upward. This correction may temper the price increase. There is a lack of full-weight Zhejiang tung oil, and quality varies. Local foreign firms have seen little trading recently. The supply of Zhejiang tung oil is scarce, and it is even more difficult to obtain full-weight oil. Most traders are unwilling to sell, and foreign firms are unwilling to buy. The market has become unusually quiet.

Measures to Save the Match Industry 224

— Gan Hongtao

Matches are a type of light industry that is essential for people’s lives and occupies an important position in industry. Several years ago, foreign matches flooded the market. Eventually, domestic match merchants worked hard to manage their businesses and find ways to improve their products, wiping out foreign match merchants who had been very active in the Chinese market. Looking at the disappearance of the Swedish match brand Phoenix from the market, one can see the general situation. Recently, the domestic match industry has also suffered from commercial downturns and market depression. Bankruptcies and liquidations have followed one after another. Without efforts to rescue the industry, it will become impossible to salvage. However, an examination of the causes of failure reveals that sluggish sales and stagnant inventory are to blame, stemming from overproduction and oversupply. At the same time, foreign matches are showing signs of activity again, being smuggled into the country to evade taxes, allowing them to be sold at low prices and severely impacting domestic goods. In addition, the match unified tax is more than double what it was two or three years ago, increasing costs. The unified tax has increased, but the selling price cannot increase accordingly, resulting in losses. For the current situation, match demand is fixed, and the only way to maintain prices without falling is to find ways to limit production. First, investigate how many matches the country needs each year and how many can be sold abroad. Then, calculate how many matches all the match factories in the country can produce each year. Compare the two to get a conclusion, and then make the overproduced amount and size of factories match, proportionally allocated to reduce. Therefore, the output of each factory has no risk of oversupply, the national output is in line with the number of sales, supply and demand can be adapted accordingly, and prices can also maintain balance. As for foreign goods imports and foreign merchants in Hong Kong, another should be used to make it so they have no foothold in the domestic. For foreign goods imports, the government must do its utmost to restrict them, impose heavy import taxes, and strictly check smuggling at each pass, so that the price cannot be lower than domestic goods when sold in China. If it sells cheaply, the result will not be a loss. For foreign merchants in the country, their manufacturing is done by machine, and the cost is lower. The government taxes must be higher than for Chinese merchants, so the selling price may not be reduced. At this critical time of crisis for the match industry, the unified match tax should ideally be temporarily reduced. If this cannot be done, then find a way to temporarily mark it down, without paying cash, and wait until the business has recovered before paying off the back payments on time. This way, cash can circulate more easily for merchants, reducing the burden, and the government can still collect taxes later. Otherwise, merchants cannot survive and are bound to fail. On the merchants' side, they should unite with each other and not engage in infighting. If they hold joint operations, etc., the price can be fixed uniformly, and those who violate the agreement will be punished. At the same time, they should also contact smoke and paper store merchants and ask them to refuse to accept foreign goods. After the matches are sold, they will be given a considerable commission, and the smoke and paper store merchants will be willing to cooperate.

Editor's Note: The match industry is indeed a business that can resist foreign goods, and we cannot bear to see it fail, so we have disclosed it. However, those who stand on invulnerable ground remain excellent in quality. It is hoped that the match industry will pay more attention to the quality of its products.
