Free Talk

Topics for Essays 225

Regarding the selection of "topics", poetry may be based on the subjective, but novels and scripts should focus on objective conditions. Poetry, in terms of form, is "non-grammatical." As long as it expresses the general meaning and is easy to recite, the lack of verbs and the omission of subjects do not matter. Anyway, there is no fear of readers being misunderstood. In substance, it is "non-intellectual" and should be exceptionally rich in emotion. Being based on the subjective means that the selected topic is simply due to feeling touched at the same time, regardless of the relationship between various things in the object. For example, in a poem, the previous paragraph writes about Ms. Wang’s vitality, and the next paragraph suddenly writes about Miss Sun’s innocence; or the front writes about Miss Sun’s sorrow, and the back suddenly writes about Ms. Wang’s troubles. It does not matter whether Ms. Wang and Miss Sun have a relationship, and how is the relationship: writing them together is only because the author is thinking about them at the same time, feeling that they are both lovely or pitiful. Therefore, in poetry, one often says a sentence about the moon, and another sentence about some flower or some bird; just describing the horror of狂风大雨, suddenly mentioning the courage and fierceness of the revolution. Haphazard collection ignores the concept of time and disregards local relations.

Novels and scripts cannot be like this. The facts written must be closely intertwined to be listed together. The so-called objectivity is to indicate the relationship between various things in the object. Therefore, the time and place of the "story" must be carefully organized. The topic does not have to form the entire story.

The selection of topics for essays is exactly in between these two, that is, on the one hand, it can be based on the subjective, and at the same time, it must take into account objective conditions. The facts written in essays must also be related to each other, and linked before and after, just like in novels and scripts. However, it is more tolerant; novels and scripts must have a certain "intention" and "focus" must be determined from the "structure". The various things written must be related to each other, and consistent before and after. Moreover, facts that are related to each other and consistent before and after may not be adopted: In order to be nervous, it must also be seen whether it is in line with the intention and structure. Essays do not need to determine a focus from the structure. In one article, they are not limited to expressing one opinion. As long as the facts are related to each other, it is okay to follow the wishes and write around the corner.

Since the various things written in essays must be linked before and after, they must be objectively examined. The facts can be adopted according to the inspiration and are not restricted by "intention" or "structure". Therefore, it can also maintain a part of the subjective relationship.

From what is said above, it can be seen that for the author's feelings, in poetry, every fact is directly and loosely related. In novels and scripts, the facts are closely linked to each other, and only the whole has a relationship with the author's feelings. In essays, the facts are linked sequentially, but the beginning and end are not necessarily directly related. At the same time, each part created by the collection of various things is related to the author's feelings.

Again Embarking on a Journey 226

— Yao Mu

—One of Brief Notes of Wandering—

Friend:

Suddenly, I woke up from a daydream.

Daydream—because in the dream, I was aware that it was a dream, and its disillusionment was also within my expectations. However, its brevity and its ending in the form of a nightmare were somewhat beyond what I imagined.

I have no regrets about the shattering of the dream; after all, daydreams are not always sweet. What I resent is its brevity—so brief that it was almost like a hallucination. I felt no panic about the transition to a nightmare, only surprise. In a real world so ordinary that it is sickening, anything with a hint of strangeness, even in a dream, is a kind of pleasure. My clever friend, do you understand this philosophy of dreams?

Not long ago, didn't you write to me with surprise, asking what kind of dream I was having? Friend, forgive me, I still cannot tell you. It's not because I have forgotten it completely after waking up, but because this dream is like a riddle. Once revealed, it loses all its flavor. At most, I can only tell you the riddle's surface.

In this dream, I am still myself, and yet not myself.

In this dream, I am doing things that I loathe and hate in my life. I am saying and writing words that praise the current authorities—words I am neither happy nor worthy to say and write. Like a lonely island, I am cut off from my old ideals and verification. In this sea of people around me, the faces, the attitudes in their speech, even the titles, the nouns, are all foreign to me—as foreign as another world. But I want to perform the monkey show of wearing a hat and robe; I want to be a parrot that can say "Guest, pour the tea." In the dream, I hear the curses of some friends, while at the same time I experience the flattery, admiration, and even jealousy of some irrelevant people. But to all of this, whether it is a curse or jealousy, I only offer a smile. In this dream, I do not loathe myself; I only mock my surroundings, because in these surroundings, I am not myself, and yet I am still myself at the same time.

Friend, perhaps you will try to apply Freud's psychoanalysis of dreams? If that's the case, you are mistaken. Contrary to Freud's philosophy of dreams, what taught me to act this way in the dream was not the "unconscious" that Freud spoke of, but precisely reason—thoroughly Kantian reason. Friend, do you feel that the more I say, the more confused you become? If I continue, I am afraid it will be like a "diamond sutra," and you will be even more clueless. But please forgive me, what I am talking about now is a dream!

However, I finally woke up from this dream.

Let me tell you some things that happened after waking up.

(Perhaps I am still dreaming now, but at least it is another dream). On a dark night, for some important business, I accompanied a friend to the dark riverside, where only a few dim lights flickered, and boarded a small steamboat that I had never taken before. The boat was filled with a load of working-class men and women, and then it set off. Looking back, the black, beast-like mountains were stretching their waists, and across the river, the mountains formed a crouching, dark shadow, watching us like monsters.

"This boat is going to the South Gate, right?" A country woman asked us repeatedly.

"Oh, probably." Actually, I was also clueless.

As soon as the boat docked, we got off, regardless of where it was. Two rickshaws carried us through the dim, quiet, straight, and narrow streets. The low shops on both sides only leaked out weak light, and the shadows of thin people dressed as workers staggered by. But I truly believed that I was walking through a dark, medieval town, not a famous city like Birmingham. After running for ten or eight miles, a small river blocked our path. I thought of the "Yin-Yang River," because behind us was a dark scene like a graveyard, and ahead of us was a display of red lights and a burst of noise, symbolizing the human world and modernity. Several "melon-skin" boats were moored by the river. We casually stepped onto one of them, and the boatman only needed to punt three times to ferry us to another world of cities.

Neon lights flashed past my eyes one by one, and the city's shadows gradually blurred. The steam whistle let out a cry, and the wheels moved slightly. My friend waved his hat at me. I shook off the hand of the nightmare that was pressing on my heart, and I felt certain that I was truly on the road to wandering. (To be continued)

Two Small Things 227

White Spirit Temple (Part 1) 228

— Yuan Chenying

When the morning bell struck seven o'clock, I was awakened by the cold wind blowing in through the round skylight on the Mongolian yurt. The sound of the trumpet, "dudu dada," entered my ears, a magnificent sound with a hint of monotonous desolation, which made me think of the ancient people in this desolate wilderness playing gongs and drums and the magnificent scene of warhorses neighing in the wind.

Stretching out my legs, which had been curled up all night in the bedding, the thick camel hair quilt (note) was just like a thin winter coat, unable to keep out the cold. I looked at everyone, and it seemed that no one wanted to get up. Although someone had added charcoal to the stove in the yurt twice during the night, it had also gone out. The cool morning wind blew in from the skylight, adding to the endless coldness inside the yurt.

Everyone was reluctant to leave the bedding that had not been warm for a night, but they were finally called and all scrambled to get up. A young man, only sixteen or seventeen years old, wearing dirty clothes, came in to light the fire, and the yurt gradually became a little warmer.

Hastily wiping my face, and then drinking the boiled water that the young man brought over, the water was turbid, with a layer of grease on top, and a hint of mutton tallow in the water. Asking the young man where he came from, he said, "I came from Guihua City to serve people here, in order to earn about ten yuan a month."

Coming out of the Mongolian yurt with the door curtain hanging, this time I could see the entire panorama of the White Spirit Temple clearly. At the foot of the mountain on the west side was the famous Inner Mongolia sacred site—the White Spirit Temple. The interconnected temples occupied a place of about a mile long, with red walls and green tiles. In the brilliant sunlight, it was dazzling. This temple differed from the temples in Guihua in that it had many lanes allowing people to enter and exit. At this time, there were very few lamas wearing red kasayas moving around. Perhaps they were chanting scriptures in the hall?

The Mongolian yurt where we lived was on the northeast side of the temple, no more than a distance of about a li. Going down the slope, you could walk into the yurt. There were about seventy Mongolian yurts, scattered in all directions, each occupying a round area of about two zhang. Wooden frames were used to support them like building a house, and thick blankets were draped on top. Thick blankets were also laid on the ground. There was a square hole in the center of the dome, which served as ventilation. The iron chimney of the stove passed through here, sending out the smoke from the stove. Military tents were interspersed between the Mongolian yurts, where the Mongolian soldiers slept. Several Mongolian yurts were lined up on the slope. Walking down the slope, you might accidentally step on them.

In front of the Mongolian yurt was a winding small river. Although it was summer, the ice had not completely melted. Inside the river were clusters of mud houses, which the people here called "Hedong," where the Han people who did business lived. Several wisps of smoke were drifting up, and it was quiet with no one in sight. (To be continued)

Old Servant 229

— Wu Guanglue

Early morning.

Faint dawn, rippling through the window, instantly illuminating the entire room with a white, shimmering light. Mo Er, lying in bed, turned over and coughed hoarsely. As his drowsy eyes made contact with the light, his body suddenly twitched as if struck by some subconscious impulse, and he immediately jumped up.

Mo Er, with bleary eyes, stumbled to the hall, opened his tired, rheum-filled eyes, and looked at the clock on the wall. Seeing that the hour hand was still pointing at six, his tense, wrinkled face returned to its usual calm state.

"Goodness—it's still early."

He sighed hoarsely. His words contained two different meanings: he was thinking about his own body, getting up so early would definitely mean insufficient rest; but in order to keep his job, he couldn't afford to get up too late. These two conflicting emotions made him sad, and he sighed from time to time. After getting up, he routinely swept the hall, corridors, steps, courtyard, etc., and wiped the tables and chairs, boiled water, and made tea... He was so busy that he was panting and sweating. He was so diligent and conscientious because he was afraid of offending his master and being fired.

He bent over, sweeping the corridors. In the quiet morning, the peculiar gloomy atmosphere of the old house made him feel even more uncomfortable. He felt as if he were in a solemn and lonely cellar. He wiped the peeling chairs, tables, lintels, and other items that had been exposed to the air for a long time. Being amidst these signs of a ruined family, he felt an increased sense of destruction and misery, and felt even more his own aging and the dark, uncertain future of his life.

"Mo Er, bring the wash water!" The young master, putting on the face of his master, hummed loudly. Although the family fortune was declining day by day, the arrogant attitude of calling servants that had been passed down from ancestors still existed. Hearing the young master's call, Mo Er immediately picked up the washbasin and went to the kitchen, panting. After picking up the washbasin, the young master's voice echoed in his ears incessantly, a dark shadow flashed before his eyes, and an unspeakable ache attacked his heart. He felt as if he could offend his master at any moment, which would jeopardize his job.

In a life of fear and hardship, the days passed one by one. But the most terrifying day in Mo Er's mind finally arrived.

On this morning, Mo Er was routinely sweeping the corridor when the young master, with a worried face, walked up to him and said in a hoarse voice, "Mo... we really hate to do this, but the times are bad, the rent is not coming in, and the taxes are high. We can't afford to support the family, so please..." The young master frowned in pain, choking on his words.

"Young master, how can this be? I am old, I have no relatives or old friends." He was overcome with grief, and old tears streamed down his face.

"Here is five yuan for travel expenses. You can go for now, maybe next year the times will be better, and you can come back."

"I won't go, young master?"

"But there's nothing I can do here."

In the end, he had no choice but to pack his simple luggage and leave the old house where he had lived for half his life. On the dusty village road, swept by the cold wind, the old man was like a lonely camel in the desert, advancing step by step on his life's journey.

"The world has changed!" He wiped away his tears and wept in a hoarse voice, "I served his old man, and I served him until he grew up. Now that I am old, he tells me to get lost. What a heartless person! The world has changed, it has changed."

His tears streamed down again.

The Death of a Person (Part 2) 230

— Hei Ying

Ya Leng was about twenty minutes away by train from this desolate dock where we were. But judging from Lao Fang's condition, he couldn't take the train; the poorly equipped train wouldn't do him any good. So, the next morning, I was assigned the task of escorting the patient to the hospital. I took the ten dollars of wages that Lao Fang had saved and the five dollars of advance payment from the boss's hand, arranged for a Malay rickshaw, and helped him with difficulty down the stairs. He sat in the rickshaw, left the pig-like boss and the pockmarked landlady, and the Singer sewing machine, and set off.

"Hospitals are not for the poor!" All the way, Lao Fang repeated this, showing his strange teeth and panting. "You don't understand, you little devil!... Cough, you are simply sending me to my funeral!"

"Don't talk nonsense!" I stopped him.

The rickshaw took us to the hospital gate, and it was already noon. Absorbed into that devilish building, Lao Fang lay on the bed in the third-class ward, his face turning an iron-blue, scary to look at, as if he was about to die. "Just lie quietly, don't think wildly, and you will get better." I patted his shoulder, comforting him.

My impression of the third-class hospital still makes me shudder when I recall it now. I don't know how many people were taken in in one large ward. The miserable sounds squeezed out of suffering filled every corner: the nurses and patients argued like enemies. There, one could often hear such shouts:

"Nurse! Hey, where did you go?"

"Bring some water, I'm dying of thirst!"

"Put up the frame, if you don't loosen the bandage for me, I'll do it myself. When I get old and rich, I'll see where you escape to!"

But the woman in white turned her head and wrinkled her nose, ignoring them and walking out.

When Lao Fang was relatively lucid, he saw this scene and told me, "Ah, did you see that? Little devil, only you would send me to the hospital. Do you think they will heal my illness? Heaven knows!" He sighed helplessly, looking up at the sky. The facts before my eyes pressed on my chest, making me unable to say anything. It wasn't until a full two hours later that I saw the Dutch doctor with his neatly trimmed mustache walk in with great authority. It was finally Lao Fang's turn. He put the stethoscope on his thin chest and kept shaking his head covered with red hair. The examination was over in five minutes. The nurse told me to follow the doctor to the outer office to get the admission certificate and pay for the medicine. It took so long that I almost missed the last night train. I said goodbye to the patient and returned to the store.

Three days later, I asked the boss to go to the hospital, but it was not allowed. "What is Lao Fang to you? He will be back soon. Don't be bewitched, go to the kitchen, it's time to cook." He said that.

"Boss, even though he is not related to me, he is still an employee of the store. Can't I go see him? And, he probably needs some money to be sent to him."

"Money? Hmph, where would he get money!"

Seeing his stubborn appearance, I was both angry and surprised, and felt that a money-loving merchant was truly beyond saving. I planned to collect some money from the store's employees for Lao Fang to send to the hospital. But when I happily gathered thirty dollars and was about to take the two o'clock train to him, regardless of whether the boss allowed it or not, the hospital's notice was sent to the store.

"What happened to Lao Fang?"

The employees fell silent, staring intently at the boss who was opening the paper. There wasn't even the sound of scissors. After he finished reading, he lowered his shaved, fat head. "He died this morning!" He said, his eyes fixed on the floor.

"It's over, use this money to buy a coffin." I said, feeling extremely sad, and I wanted to cry.

"Lao Fang was a truly pitiful fellow, he hasn't had a comfortable day in three years." One of his fellow villagers told me. "Do you know that he still has a wife and two children at home who all depend on him for support. Now, what do you think the widow and orphans will do!"

I couldn't forget him for a long time, and often when I was idle, I would think of that tall, thin man with his hunched shoulders, a kind man. He had once believed that poor people should be stronger and not get sick even for a day. This truth was proven by himself. And the landlady, who occasionally remembered that there had been a dead person in the store, always had a despicable saying on her lips:

"That dead ghost, speaking of it, still owes the store five dollars!"

Supplement to Shenbao's Local Edition

Brief Comments

From Triplets to Encouraging Births 231

— Meng Ruo

Yesterday's newspaper reported that the wife of a cobbler in Hedong, Tianjin, gave birth to triplets, all boys, and both mother and children were well. The street chief reported it to the Public Security Bureau for the record. The Public Security Bureau then sent people to express their condolences and deliver various kinds of pasta, etc.

This move by the Public Security Bureau seems to imply some meaning of encouraging births. Otherwise, giving birth to children is very common, and the authorities would definitely not send people to express their condolences or deliver food. If it is said that the authorities value it so much because it was triplets, all "boys," then that is something we dare not agree with.

Mentioning the matter of encouraging births, quite a few people have been advocating it recently. Mussolini of Italy and Hitler of Germany are two enthusiastic proponents. Everyone understands their intention in encouraging births, which is to encourage the people of the whole country to work for the nation and rush to create some little citizens to be used for future wars. Encouraging births has not yet been implemented in our country.

Our country has always boasted of its population, calling itself a large country of 400 million compatriots. It seems that there is no need to encourage births. However, this is not the case. Although our country has a large population, the number of deaths due to natural disasters and man-made disasters every year is truly astonishing. One major flood kills millions or tens of millions. One drought also kills millions or tens of millions. The number of people who sacrifice their lives under gunfire in civil wars is also impossible to count. If heaven is merciless and people are merciless, and people continue to die like this, the population of 400 million will not be difficult to turn into 300 million or 200 million in the future. This is truly worth paying attention to.

However, there are still problems with encouraging births in China at present, because there is a close relationship between population and food. As the population increases, the food supply must also increase accordingly. But in China today, there are many people and little food, and many people are starving. If births are further encouraged, it will definitely be impossible to support them. This is even more worth considering.

"Deaf" Old Man 232

— Jue Fu

——One of Old Feelings——

This old man is an outstanding figure in our Huang Town. Speaking of him, I am afraid that there is no one who lives within thirty or fifty miles of Huang Town who does not know him. But what his real name is, where his original home is, these are things that very few people can clearly say; however, because he is old, his ears are a little deaf, and he has lived in Huang Town for a long time, so we all call him "Deaf" Old Man.

He has no proper occupation, nor a decent home. His residence is in the small, dilapidated temple at the end of the market street; his only way to pass the time is to beg everywhere. Although he is so old—his beard and eyebrows are completely white, and his back is already hunched—he still seems very robust: he can drink strong wine, eat a lot of food, and walk thirty or forty miles of mountain roads every day. Whether it is sunny or rainy, as soon as the east turns white, he carries his crutch, a gourd on his back, a tattered straw bag, and his inseparable yellow dog, leaves the temple gate, and heads to the neighboring villages: it is not until the sun has set that he staggers back with a slightly drunken air.

Although he lives the same beggar's life, he is somewhat different from other beggars: usually, he does not often bother people, but whenever someone has a wedding or other joyous event, a few days before the "auspicious day," he will come uninvited. As soon as he enters the door, without him having to say anything, the host already understands his intention. At this time, the host must take out three hundred copper coins, first put them in his straw bag, then snatch his gourd and fill it with strong, unmixed wine: in addition, he must also prepare two or three kinds of delicious dishes, put them in front of him, and greet him cordially. After the host has fulfilled these "obligations," he will take out several sheets of red paper with large characters that look like printed charms from his straw bag and hand them to the host to paste everywhere. The effect of these red papers is said to be specifically used to suppress other beggars. If you don't have these, on the day of the "auspicious day," skeleton-like beggars will come in droves to make trouble, preventing you from having a good time; because he has been doing this for a long time, and he is highly qualified, he has the magical power to drive away his later peers. However, this is just a legend passed down from the mouths of old people. Whether his magical power is actually effective has never been proven by facts. However, the farmers living in this area of Huang Bo are quite satisfied and content with their lives, and they only encounter a few major wedding days in their lifetime, so they don't care much about spending a few more coins. Therefore, the life of Deaf Old Man, who lives a parasitic life, can be sustained so comfortably.

A Deaf Old Man who lives a parasitic life should, in principle, be despised and disliked, but his experience is not so unfortunate. People respect him, like him; no matter who catches a glimpse of his shadow walking into the village, they will shout excitedly: "Deaf Old Man is here, Deaf Old Man is here!" At this time, the men, women, old, and young in the house will always head towards him in unison. The children, who are not very familiar with the world, always hide like shy girls when they meet strangers, but they are not afraid of Deaf Old Man. As soon as they see Deaf Old Man walking in, they surround him in groups, asking him to tell stories and talk about news; and his belly

Page 18

also seems to have a book of stories already prepared, and the children's requests are never refused. Even if these children are so lively, he always smiles so kindly, like he is looking at his own grandchildren, patting this one on the head and that one on the head. After the stories are told, he will also have a conversation with the older generation about worldly affairs and human feelings, and talk about the fresh things he has heard and seen; and when the conversation turns to sadness, they will also sigh deeply at each other once or twice. Talking like this, he will always linger for at least an hour or two before saying goodbye and heading to another village. The old people, watching his increasingly small figure in the background, will always mutter to themselves in a daze: "He really lives a long life... really..."

I have been away from Huang Town for seven or eight years. In these long days, whether I am in books, on stage, on the road,... whenever I see an old man with white beard and eyebrows and a slightly hunched back, the first image that floats into my brain is always this Deaf Old Man.——This old man gave me too deep an impression! But I don't know if he is still living there now, and whether Huang Town, which he relies on for a living, still retains its old appearance!?

Dust and Sand 233

— Rong

When reading Tao Yuanming's poem and reaching the lines, "Life has no roots, drifting like dust on the road," I was seized by a sudden sorrow. The hand holding the book slackened, and the scene before my eyes gradually dimmed. Pages of past life turned in my mind, savoring the verses, thinking, life is truly like dust and sand, drifting and uncertain! But this dust and sand is not the light dust on the road, but the sand and soil running with the mad wind in the boundless desolate sandy land. Have you ever seen the scene of dust and soil in the northern country? When the wind rises, grains of dust and sand piece together into a thick yellow curtain, covering the clear sky entirely. Then it flutters and drifts, some floating to the rooftops, some to the treetops, some into the flowing water. No matter where it drifts or what posture it takes, it can never escape the trick of being played with by fate. Perhaps dust and soil are ignorant, perhaps they are sad? Who knows. But their drifting is real. Without a fixed home, without a fixed destination, though it is said to be freedom, the taste of a boundless future and a boundless past is probably unimaginable to those not in such a situation. When the mad wind first rises and yellow sand obscures the sky, seeing oneself so small and powerless in mid-air, and seeing countless companions being manipulated by an irresistible force, without even the power to choose, just as one clings to a withered branch, just as one settles on a rustling blade of grass, just as one falls to the ground, and one rejoices to have escaped the devil's hand of the wind, to rest one's weary life, to see again the beauty of the clear and harmonious world, suddenly another gust of wind rises, dragging one's heavy body towards an uncertain long journey without even time to breathe, so one stops again, is scattered again, without end, until this dust and sand clings to the window lattice of a certain house, or hides in a relatively quiet place, but after a short time of wind and rain, it melts, dissipates, and expires. From birth, it drifts and is unsettled, the entire life spent in the invasion of wind, frost, rain, and snow, such is the life of a grain of dust and sand. But how can such a life be so surprisingly similar to mine? You strange dust and sand, uncertain dust and sand, dust and sand played with by others!

Thinking of this, my eyes gradually closed.

I remember that in Turgenev's novel, he described a person with a weak will, saying, "I am like a stone rolling down a mountain, unable to stop myself." The dust and sand that I speak of that cannot stop itself is just like this. Every day, as I stroll back from the streets, facing the bustling traffic, I can't help but have a fantasy. I think that the people around me, before, behind, left, and right, are just like many grains of dust and sand around a grain of dust and sand, propelled by some force, involuntarily vying in the arena of fame and gain. Moreover, this wind blows ceaselessly, letting you flutter, toss, until you no longer have the strength to float with the wind, then you quietly fall from mid-air, and another layer of dust and sand buries you. In this environment, how small must one's strength appear?

Living in this world is truly an extremely heavy corvée; you must walk even if you cannot, and you must rouse yourself again when you stop. Even if you stumble and fall from exhaustion, you must pant and climb up, and then run towards the endless future. The power of the wind is too great. When will we be able to cling to a blade of grass, alongside a lively stream, and have a comfortable and beautiful dream? When will we be able to set aside our heavy burden and restore our healthy energy? On this long and obstructed journey, the traveler is too tired to endure.

Metropolitan Night Scene 234

— Luo Jia

If I were to take on the guise of a novelty seeker, with a taste for the exotic, stepping lightly in the evening breeze of a June twilight, to drift into the heart of the metropolis! That would easily elicit my admiration. For someone like me, not intimately familiar with the city, would I dare to deny everything admirable in the metropolis? Thus, I softly admired it in my heart, though I dared not let my voice of admiration attract attention.

I cultivated an air of elegance, strolling along the cement sidewalks. I bathed in the enchanting light of red and green neon lights. If I were prone to illusions, I would suspect that I had wandered into a witch's night garden, where thousands of strange and precious flowers all emitted light in the darkness, turning their colors into radiant beams. This could easily stir the heart of a man of upright and serene disposition, causing it to deviate from its orbit like a rogue planet, willing to dissolve in the seductive power of those enchanting lights! However, even if I had momentarily entertained the courage to try such a thing, it was only a fleeting thought, extinguished by my emotion of loathing. Even with the distinct types of female bodies, wrapped in a thin layer of what seemed like faint moonlight-like gauze, broadcasting the brilliance of flesh and the exotic fragrance of flesh, evenly distributed to every passerby. Interpreting this from the perspective of those floating female bodies, one feels that this unreserved display of their physical appearance possesses a unique charm. (However, this interpretation does not include the opportunity for anyone to enjoy their beauty. If, however, you are someone with a higher status and more money than them, then my explanation above will lose its effect.) Naturally, these troupes of female bodies conforming to the classical beauty of Greece paraded one by one through the night streets of the metropolis, further employing charming and graceful postures, and eyes seemingly filled with ardent tenderness, most capable of making young men with few bills in their pockets melancholic, but even more capable of arousing in stout and portly gentlemen an uncontrollable aesthetic interest. And this aesthetic interest often becomes a reality because they have many bills, enough to help it come to fruition. Thus, those seductive female bodies quickly slip into the gentleman's Studebaker car and soon appear in the rapidly playing melodies of the Gotische music, gracefully dancing on the smooth glass floor!

The metropolis is in motion, with mechanical motion and irregular motion. However, on the night streets of the metropolis, the speed of motion is intensified, the scope of motion is expanded, and the types of motion are even more complex. If you still have some patience, you can see steel wheels biting the rails, rubber wheels biting the asphalt road, neon lights biting the hearts of those wanting to go home, the brilliance of young ladies' beautiful bodies biting the desires of affectionate men, and the cheap sexual functions of street nightingales biting the interests of those sexually deprived. Thus, the night scenes of the metropolis are rendered in extremely thick paint. (If I am still a skilled speaker, then I would not say that sin serves as an important ingredient in these extremely thick paints!)

However, due to the difference between my interests and those of others, the metropolitan night scene injected me with a large dose of melancholy! Indeed, the power of capitalism is now sufficient to construct the magnificent appearance of the human world. However, I believe that what destroys the magnificent appearance of the human world is still capitalism itself. Not only is it futile, but it is also superfluous. Thus, I suspect that the melancholy tune of my whistle is singing a funeral song for this century.

Home of the Unemployed 235

— Ye Fei

A simple bedroom, with only a wooden plank bed, a pile of old bedding and a few worn-out clothes scattered on it. In the corner, a child was sleeping. Two stools were casually placed beside the bed. An old half-table was placed in front of the window, but a Western-style stove nearby was not lit. The whitewash on the surrounding walls had all turned blackish-gray. The air in the room was deathly still and terrifying. At that time, Pinghua was sitting at the old half-table by the window, picking up a pen to write a letter to a cousin, asking him to find him a job in Hankou, but when he thought of his cousin's snobbish face, and the insults that Yunqian had suffered when she visited his home last time, he tore the eight-line letter paper on which he had just written two lines to shreds, and scraps of paper flew all over the floor. He suddenly grabbed his hair with both hands desperately, and a pair of lifeless eyeballs stared out the window, watching several small sparrows perching on the electric wire, preening their wings, hunger and grief intertwined in his mind!

"Ah!" With a sound, the child woke up on the bed, and Yunqian hurriedly picked him up from the pile of broken quilts. That green, one-year-old child was also so thin that he only had a piece of skin left. Even when he cried, there were only those weak twitchings and low voices. His neck was thin and soft, truly like a dying child.

"Child... you were born with... a bitter fate, so... you were cast into... such... a mommy and daddy..." As she spoke, two lines of bitter tears surged like a mountain torrent, and the tears fell from her face onto the child's cheek. She looked at the child, pressed a tear-soaked, thin face tightly against the child's face, but the child still cried vigorously. "Child... Mom's milk is dry. Child! Mom has no food to eat, so where is there milk for you to eat!"

He glanced sadly at the child and his wife, thinking: they are truly suffering. Since Yunqian married me,

Page 19

she hasn't had a single day of peace. Less than a year after our marriage, I lost my job, and now there's another child. For nearly a year of unemployment, everything that could be pawned has been pawned, and everything that could be sold has been sold. Now there's nothing left that's worth anything. I've been running around everywhere, and I've been to almost all the relatives and friends' places, but the result has only been cold insults and contemptuous mockery! But since I can't find a job and I have nowhere to borrow money, how can I continue to survive? Just this three-story attic we live in costs four yuan a month in rent. We're already three months behind, and the landlord's face is not as kind as before. I can see that he's about to issue an eviction order soon. But our stomachs haven't had a good meal in two days, and now we really can't bear it anymore. The clear water in our chests just bubbles straight up, and that sour and sweet taste is harder to bear than anything!

"Tch! This... this snobbish world!" He slammed the table hatefully.

"The day before yesterday, I saw an advertisement in the newspaper for female clerks, and I tried it out. Their qualifications for the exam were just beauty in appearance and youth, so the result of my test was said to be passing, but today I received their notice saying that they still need a 200 yuan guarantee..." Yunqian thought of the exam she took the other day and couldn't help but feel angry. Then she threw a crumpled letter in front of Pinghua!

"These are all swindlers!" Pinghua grabbed the letter and tore it up.

The two were silent again, and sorrow and pain pressed tightly in the room. The child's crying also stopped at some point.

"Ping, I still want to go to the employment agency and ask if anyone wants to hire a wet nurse or nanny. Let me do it and see if it will maintain our current life. Anyway, poor people don't need to care about face anymore. Even their lives can't be guaranteed!" She said a string of words, followed by two long strings of tears, but she still wanted to force a smile so that Pinghua wouldn't be too sad!

"But what about the child?" Pinghua couldn't help crying either. He suddenly hugged Yunqian and pressed his face against her disheveled hair: "Yun, you've suffered. How can I let you suffer such humiliation?"

"I think we should send the child to the orphanage! On the one hand, it will preserve his little life, and at the same time, you and I can find some odd jobs to do."

"Yun!" He looked at her with tears in his eyes and cried out, but couldn't say a word of comfort.

"Ping! What's wrong?" She sadly wiped away his tears, forgetting the hunger in her stomach from not eating for two days. Only pain and sorrow occupied them both.

Broadcasting News 238

The Shanghai Opera Company, which has long been famous in the broadcasting world, was rumored to be dissolved some time ago. After investigation by all parties, it is completely inconsistent with the facts. Since its establishment last year, the company has been headed by Liu Hengzhi as the president, and the company's affairs have also been presided over by him alone. Now, in order to make the group organization more solid and seek the development of the company's affairs, Mr. Liu specially invited Yan Hua, the former leader of Xinhua News Agency, and others to jointly establish the Shanghai Opera Company's Board of Directors as the company's basic organization. Liu Hengzhi, Wang Yintai, Xu Jinxian, Yan Deyi, and Yan Hua serve as directors. Yesterday, the inaugural meeting of the Board of Directors was held at the Xinxin Company Broadcasting Station. All directors attended and performed the ceremony as scheduled. The organization regulations of the Board of Directors and the company's articles of association were immediately passed. Subsequently, Xu Jinxian was elected as the chairman of the board, and many proposals for the company's affairs were discussed. Yan Hua and Liu Hengzhi have now been officially hired by the Board of Directors as the company's principal and vice leaders, responsible for researching all artistic development matters. Wang Yintai and Yan Deyi were hired as the principal and vice directors of the General Affairs Department, responsible for studying all company affairs. Ms. Zhang Wen was also hired as the music conductor, and the company address was set at No. 19, Qingdao Road, this port. At a specified time every day, the staff is gathered to intensify training. It is heard that the company will formally solicit members and first give them considerable training? Once the training is mature, it is planned to hold a large-scale opera performance on stage.

The Broadcasting World semi-monthly publication, published and distributed by the Broadcasting World Publishing House, No. 71, Lane 353, Xinzha Road, this port, the inaugural issue has been published on the 10th. The publication is edited by Fan Songyao, with wonderful and insightful content, and has many photos of broadcasting musicians, all in color and finely printed. The publication is a good companion for those who own radios. The retail price is five cents per copy. All magazine companies and newspaper vendors sell it. It is also heard that the company now plans to solicit 5,000 basic subscribers. The annual cost, including postage, is only one yuan and a corner.

Movie News

News from Yi Hua 239

Bu Wancang, the director of Yi Hua, is good at socializing and has many foreign friends. Yesterday, when he was directing a rural housing scene for his film "Triumphant Song," four or five of his foreign friends came to visit.

Wu Weiyun, the cinematographer for "The Storm," is fond of stage shows. Recently, he often goes to the Hebei Theater alone during his breaks from work.

In "Hero of the Times," there is a dog performance scene. Directors Ying Yunwei and Qin Tong, who have two well-trained and understanding dogs, were specially requested to lend them. On the day of filming, Qin Tong and his son brought each dog to the company. In front of everyone, they demonstrated the usual training they gave the dogs, instructing them to perform for everyone. He told the dog to sit on a sofa and bow to everyone. The dog actually sat very properly and bowed to everyone. Qin Tong did not tell it to stop, and it dared not stop. It seems Qin Tong put a lot of effort into training this dog.

The interior scenes for "The Storm" will be filmed after a large set from the International Grand Theater is completed, then they will go to Qingdao to shoot exterior scenes.

"At the Beginning of Life" has been showing at the Jincheng Grand Theater since the fifth. In those five days, the total number of viewers was 22,571, with an average of more than 4,500 people watching each day.

Yuan Meiyun will shine in "The Storm."

Miss Zhou Xuan: From the Music Scene to the Silver Screen 240

— Photo by Qichang

The Profile of Shi Chao, an Actor from Diantong 241

Shi Chao—one of Diantong's "newcomers." He is from Beiping, and one of the male leads in "Goddess of Freedom." He has a handsome and pretty face, fluent Mandarin, and a cheerful demeanor. Upon meeting him, you will feel his humble and amiable manners, and his warm and sincere friendship. If you spend a long time with him, he will also joke around with you.

He has excellent mimicking skills. He can cleverly imitate Manager Ma Dejian's attitude and Factory Director Situ Yimin's seriousness. He can even imitate the unique postures of foreign movie stars such as Paul Muni and Wallace Beery perfectly. When he arrives at the film set, the atmosphere becomes lively. He constantly makes melodious sounds from his mouth, singing and humming tunes. At the same time, he can also stir up interest on the basketball court. The Diantong basketball team is well-organized, and he can be said to be one of the most influential members. After each game, his analysis of the game and the players' experiences always lead to significant improvements.

Lianhua's Sound Film Recording Equipment 242

The production of Lianhua's sound films is something that film enthusiasts and the entire film industry are extremely concerned about. Precisely because of this, Lianhua must be particularly cautious about the production of sound films. At the same time, Lianhua's colleagues have a kind of ambition for sound film production: "If we don't make a sound, we will startle the world with a single sound." Therefore, sufficient time must be allowed for the preparation of the script.

However, although Lianhua's sound films have not yet been produced, Lianhua's sound film recording equipment has already begun working. All the music and sound effects for "Carefree Gentleman" were recorded by their own recording equipment. The clarity and loudness of the sound have been proven by facts, so there is no need to elaborate further.

However, that was only the first trial. We believe that the results of "Autumn Fan and Bright Lamp," which is currently in preparation for sound design, will definitely be even more perfect, without any doubt.

Mr. Chen Tan Chang has been in the United States for more than ten years, and has served as a sound engineer at the Victor Talking Machine Company. After returning to China, he is now employed by the Lianhua General Film Studio as the chief sound engineer. The sound equipment recently purchased by Lianhua from the United States has been tested by him and has achieved excellent results. The photo on the left is of Mr. Chen.

Shen Bao Architectural Weekly

Hospital Design in Modern Architecture 243

— Dao

At 8 PM on June 6th, the Hong Kong University Alumni Association of this port held a meeting at the Bankers Club. Many famous figures from China and abroad attended. Marquis G. G. Cihadini Cesi, Secretary of the Italian Embassy, also spared time to attend. Mr. Wang Daoan presided over the meeting and specially invited Mr. CHelazzi to give a lecture on "Hospital Design in Modern Architecture." He explained in detail the new plans for hospital construction. Mr. Chelazzi is a famous architect who recently won the design competition for the British Concession Bureau Hospital in Tianjin. This lecture will surely make a significant contribution to the modern architectural world. The original manuscript of the speech is translated into Chinese and disclosed below:

If someone asks me to define modern architecture, I can say without hesitation that modern architecture must contain the following balances:

(1) Balance of lines and colors—creating beauty with simplicity and unadornment.

(2) Balance of interior and exterior—the exterior should evoke pleasure, while the interior should be practical.

(3) Balance of light and shadow—fully utilizing light when it is beneficial, while providing a barrier when it is harmful.

(4) Balance of ventilation—ensuring sufficient circulation of wind and air when needed.

Modern architecture not only focuses on the surface appearance, but also seeks utilization in all aspects with creative art. Therefore, modern hospital architecture uses new methods to provide comfort and convenience.

Taking the Tianjin British Concession Hospital that I designed as an example, it is designed based on simplicity, order, straightforwardness, and aerodynamics. In recent years, China has indeed made great progress in construction, but the construction of hospitals—especially in the interior—is urgently needed. When planning a hospital in China, in addition to common problems, one must also consider the local conditions. In my personal opinion, the most important thing is the climate. In winter, the wind direction in Tianjin is north and northwest, and in summer it is southeast. Therefore, I placed the wards in the south and the working areas in the north. In this way, the wards have sufficient air circulation in the summer and are not attacked by the cold north wind in all seasons. As for sunlight, I placed the wards in such a position that they can fully benefit from the sunlight. The wards are connected to balconies, so they can block the hot summer sun, while the winter sun can shine into the balcony without obstruction.

According to thirty years of records, the average minimum temperature in Tianjin is 2.92 degrees Fahrenheit, and the lowest is four degrees below zero. Therefore, I think it is best to set the indoor temperature at 66 degrees. In order to reduce heat transfer through the outer walls, the outer walls are constructed with a layer of six-inch hollow bricks, a layer of four-inch hollow tiles, with a five-inch air layer in between. In order to further reduce heat loss, the windows are constructed with double layers and balanced frames. The advantage of this type of window is that it can be opened as much as possible, and there are no vertical bars, so light can penetrate more fully.

In addition to the hospital itself, there are also nurses' residences, manager's residences, and doctor's residences, all built in another part, not connected to the hospital. The servants' residences are in the west. The morgue is in the southwest, with a separate entrance.

In my opinion, the scenery around the hospital deserves special attention. Trees, lawns, green sidewalks, fountains, ponds, and seats are all very necessary.

Generally speaking, hospital buildings should be concentrated in one place, because the land occupied and the expenses incurred are more economical than if they are scattered.

Each floor of the ward is equipped with a sliding door, leading to a soiled linen chute. All soiled linen is collected in this chute and transported directly to the laundry room on the ground floor. After the soiled linen is washed, it is placed in a linen delivery room near the elevator and directly distributed to the linen storage rooms on each floor. Each floor also has a garbage chute, which leads directly to the incinerator for incineration. The kitchen is on the top floor, because experience tells us that if the kitchen is below, the smell will be very harmful to patients, even if all methods are exhausted to avoid it.

The operating room is designed in the north, so that the operating table can receive very even light during the day. Air circulation and heating are a very serious issue. After careful research, it was decided to use a separate heating and cooling system, first disinfecting the air with heat, then cooling it to the appropriate temperature and sending it to each operating room.

In short, the design of modern hospitals includes many engineering and architectural problems, which are becoming increasingly complex with the advancement of medicine. Those engaged in this design work should regard their work as sacred, because they may also be indirect tools for benefiting mankind.

Research on the Trends of Residential Architecture in Shanghai (Part 2) 244

— Liu Zhongchao

Currently, the construction of two- or three-story lane houses with two buildings has been reduced. The latest style popular on the market is the two- or three-story, two-section style. The characteristic is to deepen the living room on the ground floor by five or six feet, and divide it into front and rear rooms with a false door. The rear room can also be used as a dining room. The height of the rooms is reduced by about one foot compared to before. The space at the top of the building is used as a storage room, which is very convenient for living. However, the rent is one-tenth or one-fifth more expensive than the ordinary style. Two-story houses rent for 60 or 70 yuan a month, and three-story houses rent for about 90 yuan. It is only suitable for the middle class, and the lower middle class cannot enjoy it. Moreover, once old-style lane houses or houses with large gardens are demolished, they are rebuilt into new styles. If this continues, there will inevitably be an oversupply of houses, and the lower middle class who now live in old-style lane houses will inevitably experience panic in the future. Even now, looking at the advertisements for rent and rent reduction in the newspapers, it can be seen that it is gradually declining. Therefore, there is still a need for reform in future styles. Judging from the current situation, there are roughly two methods. One is to abolish the front patio, and retract the second and third floors by six or seven feet, so that the distance from the front lane houses can still maintain the current width. The distance on the ground floor seems too close. If the roof surface let out by the upper floors is converted into a glass roof, the light and air will still not be affected. Now, many lane houses, and many are new styles, do not have patios, but only have a door sleeve to reach the lane. Also, Su and Guang tailor shops in the lane often build a glass top on the patio. The two can be the model for the above style. The other is to shrink the entire house into a small residence. Taking independent villas as an example, the newly built ones, such as those on Fulu Li Road, Yuyuan Road, and the downtown area, are mostly small villas. If there were large villas like those on Julu Road, investors would never build them. It can be seen that lane houses have a trend to shrink. As for interior and exterior decoration and equipment, there is also a trend towards simplicity, because the existing spatial lane houses are mostly rich and gorgeous. The newly built independent villas are mostly flat-topped and three-dimensional, and the pointed-topped ones are in the Spanish style. This style saves labor and materials, and is also very beautiful, and is welcomed by people, so it can be popular. The trend of apartment buildings is roughly that small-scale ones (including six or eight houses) have a very large capacity and room area, and the decoration and equipment are also rich and luxurious, extremely extravagant, such as the recently built Grosvenor apt and Ostrid apt on Myers Road and the apartment at the corner of Avenue Joffre and Avenue Haig. This is because the history of apartments in Shanghai is only more than ten years, and most of them were built in the last three or five years, and are mostly new styles. Because of their comfort, convenience, and safety, they are very popular among the rich—especially foreigners. Therefore, in large apartments, the capacity of each house is increased and the number is reduced, in order to facilitate rental. For example, the newly built Yue Tuck apt on Difeng Road has twelve large houses and fourteen small houses. The large houses are all rented out, and most of the small houses cannot be rented out. It can be seen that as long as it is large, even if the rent is high, it will not affect it, just like the increasingly strange architecture of Shanghai's dance halls and cinemas a few years ago. As for the future trend, it will inevitably be the same as lane houses or independent villas. (The above description is limited to city houses. Private self-built residences are not included in this example.)

Architectural Jargon (15) 245

— Mei Zhenhuan

——Regarding Usage on the Construction Site——

Hinges—In our country, which is loudly advocating domestic products, the monthly import of foreign goods that flood the market is truly astonishing, especially in the construction industry. For example, the hinges (Butt or Hinge) used on construction sites are mostly imported products (it can be said that there are no domestic products). They are metal objects with a rotating property that are essential for doors or windows, with two connected parts. Some elaborate ones have springs. (Writing this, I report a gratifying piece of news, that Chinese people can also make iron windows and iron doors that are more elaborate in construction.)

Bolts—Bolts are used to prevent doors or windows from suddenly opening and closing due to strong winds. They are also imported products. There is a type called French bolts, which can be closed at the top and bottom of the door or window, with a rotating handle in the middle.

Baskets—What is most difficult to eliminate on the construction site is garbage. It is difficult to become a construction site without garbage, because the amount of garbage is transformed from sawdust, shavings, and cement chips that have been removed from the cement casing. However, to clear the garbage, it is necessary to use small workers (the head is called a small worker). The small worker must use a broom and a basket. This basket is used to carry any unusable waste.

Rope for the Basket—This is the rope that is used to wear the basket.

Pole for the Basket—This is the carrying pole for the basket, which is made of thick bamboo.

Sawdust—The wood that is sawed off the wood with a saw is called sawdust.

Shavings—The wood that is planed off the wood with a plane is called shavings.

Wood Scraps—When using a copper stick to pry a shell plate, the broken pieces of wood are called wood scraps. Regarding wood scraps, sawdust, and shavings, there are people who specialize in this business on the construction site who come to bargain and sell them. This is the utilization of waste on the construction site. For construction sites with relatively large projects, the income from the transaction of these three is considerable. There are also people on the construction site who come to buy empty cement bags and unused scrap iron (detailed above).

Steel Bar—Steel bars (Steel Stice) are the most widely used tools on the construction site, such as for prying shell plates, pulling out wire nails, and carrying heavy objects.

Dormer Window—Ordinary lane houses or street houses were originally built as two-story styles, but the second landlord hopes to produce more rent, so regardless of whether the third tenant is comfortable, he builds a loft on the original two stories, which becomes three stories, but the air is inevitably suffocating. The second landlord opens a skylight (Sky Light) on the roof, or builds a small house like a roof with "one side leaking water." This is the dormer window. As for the word "tiger," it probably refers to the position of the window, which resembles the tiger's big mouth, hence the name.

"One Side Leaking Water"—This sentence "one side leaking water" is also a habitual phrase spoken by many workers on the construction site. It means that only one side of the position leaks rain, and leaking water is another name for water seepage.

Old Steward—If someone wants to visit a friend on the construction site, or needs to find someone to help with a certain matter, then what you see on the construction site are many mud workers and carpenters, but of course you cannot call them workers, or randomly call them names like "Hey you" because most of the workers are ignorant. You must give them some small advantages, so you might as well call the workers "Old Steward." In fact, the three words "Old Steward" can be applied on the construction site from the foreman and boss down to the small "student" apprentices, and is not necessarily limited to the workers who do the knocking and fiddling.

Partition—The meaning of partition is a partition made of tongue-and-groove boards or other boards such as Jian Song boards. For example, in ordinary lane houses or street houses, the living room or floor is divided into two with a partition. The former is called the front living room front floor, and the latter is called the back living room back floor. This type of partition is most often used in small inns for small, pigeon-cage-like rooms.

Curb Stone—The edge of the sidewalk on the road is inlaid with stone material, which is the curb stone. The first hand procedure for the end of the house is based on the height of the curb stone or the back of the road as the standard for the height of the foundation of the house, so the curb stone (Curt) or the back of the road has become the first gate for starting construction on the construction site. (To be continued)
